href="/wiki/File:Eurostar_map.svg" class="image"><img alt="Eurostar map.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Eurostar_map.svg/290px-Eurostar_map.svg.png" decoding="async" /></a></td></tr>\n</tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><i><b>Eurostar</b></i> is an international <a href="/wiki/High-speed_rail" title="High-speed rail">high-speed rail</a> service connecting the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> with <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>. Most Eurostar trains travel through the <a href="/wiki/Channel_Tunnel" title="Channel Tunnel">Channel Tunnel</a> between the United Kingdom and France, owned and operated separately by <a href="/wiki/Getlink" title="Getlink">Getlink</a>.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> terminus is <a href="/wiki/St_Pancras_railway_station" title="St Pancras railway station">London St Pancras International</a>; the other British calling points are <a href="/wiki/Ebbsfleet_International_railway_station" title="Ebbsfleet International railway station">Ebbsfleet International</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ashford_International_railway_station" title="Ashford International railway station">Ashford International</a> in <a href="/wiki/Kent" title="Kent">Kent</a>. Intermediate calling points in France are <a href="/wiki/Calais-Fr%C3%A9thun_station" title="Calais-Fr\xc3\xa9thun station">Calais-Fr\xc3\xa9thun</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lille-Europe_station" title="Lille-Europe station">Lille-Europe</a>. Trains to <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a> terminate at <a href="/wiki/Gare_du_Nord" title="Gare du Nord">Gare du Nord</a>. Trains to Belgium and the Netherlands serve <a href="/wiki/Brussels-South_railway_station" title="Brussels-South railway station">Brussels-South</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rotterdam_Centraal_station" title="Rotterdam Centraal station">Rotterdam Centraal</a>, before terminating at <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Centraal_station" title="Amsterdam Centraal station">Amsterdam Centraal</a>. Additionally, in France there are direct services from London to <a href="/wiki/Marne-la-Vall%C3%A9e%E2%80%93Chessy_station" title="Marne-la-Vall\xc3\xa9e\xe2\x80\x93Chessy station">Marne-la-Vall\xc3\xa9e\xe2\x80\x93Chessy</a> (<a href="/wiki/Disneyland_Paris" title="Disneyland Paris">Disneyland Paris</a>) and seasonal direct services to southern France (Lyon, Avignon and Marseille) in summer, and to the French Alps in winter.\n</p><p>The service is operated by 11 <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_373" title="British Rail Class 373">Class 373/1 trainsets</a>, each with 18 coaches, and 17 <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_374" title="British Rail Class 374">Class 374 trainsets</a>, each with 16 coaches. The trains run at up to 320 kilometers per hour (200&#160;mph) on high-speed lines. The <a href="/wiki/LGV_Nord" title="LGV Nord">LGV Nord</a> high-speed line in France opened before Eurostar services began in 1994, and newer lines enabling faster journeys were added later: <a href="/wiki/HSL_1" title="HSL 1">HSL 1</a> in Belgium and <a href="/wiki/High_Speed_1" title="High Speed 1">High Speed 1</a> in south-east England. The French and Belgian parts of the network are shared with Paris\xe2\x80\x93Brussels <a href="/wiki/Thalys" title="Thalys">Thalys</a> services and <a href="/wiki/TGV" title="TGV">TGV</a> trains.\n</p><p>Eurostar is operated by <a href="/wiki/Eurostar_International_Limited" title="Eurostar International Limited">Eurostar International Limited</a> (EIL), jointly owned by <a href="/wiki/SNCF" title="SNCF">SNCF</a>, the national railway of France (55%), investment firms (40%), and the <a href="/wiki/National_Railway_Company_of_Belgium" title="National Railway Company of Belgium">National Railway Company of Belgium</a> (5%).\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" href="#HSL_1_(Belgium)"><span class="tocnumber">2.3</span> <span class="toctext">HSL 1 (Belgium)</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-16"><a href="#High_Speed_1_(United_Kingdom)"><span class="tocnumber">2.4</span> <span class="toctext">High Speed 1 (United Kingdom)</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17"><a href="#Services"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Services</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-18"><a href="#Frequency"><span class="tocnumber">3.1</span> <span class="toctext">Frequency</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-19"><a href="#Fares"><span class="tocnumber">3.2</span> <span class="toctext">Fares</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-20"><a href="#Service_connections"><span class="tocnumber">3.3</span> <span class="toctext">Service connections</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-21"><a class="toclevel-2 tocsection-28"><a href="#Fleet_details"><span class="tocnumber">4.1</span> <span class="toctext">Fleet details</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-29"><a 374</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-33"><a href="#Past_fleet"><span class="tocnumber">4.3</span> <span class="toctext">Past fleet</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-34"><a href="#Possible_use_of_double-deck_trains"><span class="tocnumber">4.4</span> <span class="toctext">Possible use of double-deck trains</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-35"><a href="#Accidents,_incidents_and_events"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Accidents, incidents and events</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-36"><a href="#Minor_incidents"><span class="tocnumber">5.1</span> <span class="toctext">Minor incidents</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-37"><a href="#1996"><span class="tocnumber">5.2</span> <span class="toctext">1996</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-38"><a href="#2000"><span class="tocnumber">5.3</span> <span class="toctext">2000</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-39"><a href="#2007"><span class="tocnumber">5.4</span> <span class="toctext">2007</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-40"><a href="#2009"><span class="tocnumber">5.5</span> <span class="toctext">2009</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-41"><a href="#2010"><span class="tocnumber">5.6</span> <span class="toctext">2010</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-42"><a href="#2011"><span class="tocnumber">5.7</span> <span class="toctext">2011</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-43"><a href="#Possible_developments"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Possible developments</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-44"><a href="#Stratford_International_station"><span class="tocnumber">6.1</span> <span class="toctext">Stratford International station</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-45"><a href="#Regional_Eurostar"><span class="tocnumber">6.2</span> <span class="toctext">Regional Eurostar</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-46"><a href="#High_Speed_2"><span class="tocnumber">6.3</span> <span class="toctext">High Speed 2</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-47"><a href="#LGV_Picardie"><span class="tocnumber">6.4</span> <span class="toctext">LGV Picardie</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-48"><a href="#New_destinations"><span class="tocnumber">6.5</span> <span class="toctext">New destinations</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-49"><a href="#Operational_difficulties_with_cross-border_trains"><span class="tocnumber">6.5.1</span> <span class="toctext">Operational difficulties with cross-border trains</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-50"><a href="#French_high-speed_rail_expansion"><span class="tocnumber">6.5.2</span> <span class="toctext">French high-speed rail expansion</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-51"><a href="#Eurostar_expansion"><span class="tocnumber">6.5.3</span> <span class="toctext">Eurostar expansion</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-52"><a href="#Southern_France"><span class="tocnumber">6.5.4</span> <span class="toctext">Southern France</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-53"><a href="#Netherlands"><span class="tocnumber">6.5.5</span> <span class="toctext">Netherlands</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-54"><a href="#Competition"><span class="tocnumber">6.6</span> <span class="toctext">Competition</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-55"><a href="#Ridership"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Ridership</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-56"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-57"><a href="#Bibliography"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Bibliography</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-58"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Conception_and_planning">Conception and planning</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Conception and planning">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Channel_Tunnel" title="Channel Tunnel">Channel Tunnel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Getlink" title="Getlink">Getlink</a>, and <a href="/wiki/TransManche_Link" title="TransManche Link">TransManche Link</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eurotunnel_schema_(empty_service).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Eurotunnel_schema_%28empty_service%29.svg/220px-Eurotunnel_schema_%28empty_service%29.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="88" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Eurotunnel_schema_%28empty_service%29.svg/330px-Eurotunnel_schema_%28empty_service%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Eurotunnel_schema_%28empty_service%29.svg/440px-Eurotunnel_schema_%28empty_service%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="595" data-file-height="238" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eurotunnel_schema_(empty_service).svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A typical cross-section of the <a href="/wiki/Channel_Tunnel" title="Channel Tunnel">Channel Tunnel</a>. A service tunnel was constructed in between the twin rail tunnels.</div></div></div>\n<p>The history of Eurostar can be traced to the choice in 1986 of a rail tunnel to provide a cross-channel link between Britain and France.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> A previous attempt to construct a tunnel between the two nations had begun in 1974, but was quickly aborted. Construction began afresh in 1988. <a href="/wiki/Getlink" title="Getlink">Eurotunnel</a> was created to manage and own the tunnel, which was finished in 1993, the official opening taking place on 6 May 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_openingceremony_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_openingceremony-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In addition to the tunnel\'s <a href="/wiki/Eurotunnel_Shuttle" title="Eurotunnel Shuttle">shuttle trains</a> carrying cars and lorries between <a href="/wiki/Folkestone" title="Folkestone">Folkestone</a> and <a href="/wiki/Calais" title="Calais">Calais</a>, the tunnel opened up the possibility of through passenger and freight train services between places further afield.<sup id="cite_ref-EuroTun_His_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EuroTun_His-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/British_Rail" title="British Rail">British Rail</a> and SNCF contracted with Eurotunnel to use half the tunnel\'s capacity for this purpose. In 1987, Britain, France and Belgium set up an International Project Group to specify a train to provide an international high-speed passenger service through the tunnel. France had been operating high-speed TGV services since 1981, and had begun construction of a new high-speed line between Paris and the Channel Tunnel, LGV Nord; French TGV technology was chosen as the basis for the new trains. An order for 30 trainsets, to be manufactured in France but with some British and Belgian components, was placed in December 1989.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> On 20 June 1993, the first Eurostar test train travelled through the tunnel to the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-Eurost_His_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eurost_His-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Various technical difficulties in running the new trains on British tracks were quickly overcome.<sup id="cite_ref-Eurobreakdown_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eurobreakdown-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Launch_of_service">Launch of service</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Launch of service">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eurostar.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Eurostar.svg/220px-Eurostar.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Eurostar.svg/330px-Eurostar.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Eurostar.svg/440px-Eurostar.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="367" data-file-height="287" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eurostar.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The original Eurostar logo used from 1994 until 2011.</div></div></div>\n<p>On 14 November 1994, Eurostar services began running from <a href="/wiki/Waterloo_International_railway_station" title="Waterloo International railway station">London Waterloo International</a> station in London, to <a href="/wiki/Paris_Gare_du_Nord" class="mw-redirect" title="Paris Gare du Nord">Paris Gare du Nord</a> in Paris, and <a href="/wiki/Brussels-South_railway_station" title="Brussels-South railway station">Brussels-South railway station</a> in Brussels.<sup id="cite_ref-EuroTun_His_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EuroTun_His-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-waterloovid_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-waterloovid-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Watlooguardi_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Watlooguardi-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> The train service started with a limited <i>Discovery</i> service; the full daily service started from 28 May 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-Rail_Chronology:_Eurostar_services_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rail_Chronology:_Eurostar_services-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1995, Eurostar was achieving an average end-to-end speed of 171.5&#160;km/h (106.6&#160;mph) from London to Paris.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\nOn 8 January 1996, Eurostar launched services from a second railway station in the UK when <a href="/wiki/Ashford_International_railway_station" title="Ashford International railway station">Ashford International</a> was opened.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 23 September 2003, passenger services began running on the first completed section of <a href="/wiki/High_Speed_1" title="High Speed 1">High Speed 1</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Eurost_His_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eurost_His-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Following a high-profile glamorous opening ceremony<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> and a large advertising campaign,<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> on 14 November 2007, Eurostar services in London transferred from Waterloo to the extended and extensively refurbished <a href="/wiki/London_St_Pancras_International" class="mw-redirect" title="London St Pancras International">London St Pancras International</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-transpancras_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-transpancras-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div style="clear:left;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Records_achieved">Records achieved</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Records achieved">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Faster_Tomorrow.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Faster_Tomorrow.jpg/220px-Faster_Tomorrow.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="129" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Faster_Tomorrow.jpg/330px-Faster_Tomorrow.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Faster_Tomorrow.jpg/440px-Faster_Tomorrow.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="939" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Faster_Tomorrow.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Eurostar relocated from <a href="/wiki/Waterloo_International_railway_station" title="Waterloo International railway station">London Waterloo International station</a> to <a href="/wiki/St_Pancras_International_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="St Pancras International railway station">London St Pancras International station</a> in November 2007.</div></div></div>\n<p>The Channel Tunnel used by Eurostar services holds the record for having the longest underwater section of any tunnel in the world,<sup id="cite_ref-Daily_Post_2006_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Daily_Post_2006-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> and it is the third-longest railway tunnel (behind the Seikan tunnel and the Gotthard Base Tunnel) in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 30 July 2003, a Eurostar train set a new British <a href="/wiki/List_of_vehicle_speed_records" title="List of vehicle speed records">speed record</a> of 334.7&#160;km/h (208.0&#160;mph) on the first section of the "High Speed 1" railway between the Channel Tunnel,<sup id="cite_ref-Eurost_His_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eurost_His-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-waterloovid_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-waterloovid-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> and Fawkham Junction in north Kent, two months before official public services began running.\n</p><p>On 16 May 2006, Eurostar set a new record for the longest non-stop high-speed journey, a distance of 1,421 kilometres (883&#160;mi) from <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> to <a href="/wiki/Cannes" title="Cannes">Cannes</a> taking 7 hours 25 minutes.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 4 September 2007, a record-breaking train left Paris Gare du Nord at 10:44 (09:44 <a href="/wiki/British_Summer_Time" title="British Summer Time">BST</a>) and reached London St Pancras International in 2&#160;hours 3&#160;minutes 39 seconds,<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> carrying journalists and railway workers. This record trip was also the first passenger-carrying arrival at the new <a href="/wiki/St_Pancras_railway_station" title="St Pancras railway station">London St Pancras International station</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> On 20 September 2007, Eurostar broke another record when it completed the journey from Brussels to London in 1&#160;hour 43&#160;minutes.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Regional_Eurostar_and_Nightstar">Regional Eurostar and Nightstar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Regional Eurostar and Nightstar">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eurostars_at_waterloo_international.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Eurostars_at_waterloo_international.jpg/220px-Eurostars_at_waterloo_international.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Eurostars_at_waterloo_international.jpg/330px-Eurostars_at_waterloo_international.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Eurostars_at_waterloo_international.jpg/440px-Eurostars_at_waterloo_international.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1632" data-file-height="1232" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eurostars_at_waterloo_international.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A pair of <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_373" title="British Rail Class 373">Eurostar trains</a> at the former <a href="/wiki/Waterloo_International_railway_station" title="Waterloo International railway station">London Waterloo International</a></div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Regional_Eurostar" title="Regional Eurostar">Regional Eurostar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nightstar_(train)" title="Nightstar (train)">Nightstar (train)</a></div>\n<p>The original proposals for Eurostar included direct services to Paris and Brussels from cities north of London: <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Piccadilly_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Manchester Piccadilly railway station">Manchester Piccadilly</a> via <a href="/wiki/Birmingham_New_Street_railway_station" title="Birmingham New Street railway station">Birmingham New Street</a> on the <a href="/wiki/West_Coast_Main_Line" title="West Coast Main Line">West Coast Main Line</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leeds_railway_station" title="Leeds railway station">Leeds</a> and <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Central_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Glasgow Central railway station">Glasgow Central</a> via <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Waverley_railway_station" title="Edinburgh Waverley railway station">Edinburgh Waverley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_railway_station" title="Newcastle railway station">Newcastle</a> and <a href="/wiki/York_railway_station" title="York railway station">York</a> on the <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_Main_Line" title="East Coast Main Line">East Coast Main Line</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Seven 14-coach "North of London" Eurostar trains for these <a href="/wiki/Regional_Eurostar" title="Regional Eurostar">Regional Eurostar</a> services were built, but these services never came to fruition. Predicted journey times of almost nine hours for Glasgow to Paris at the time of growth of low-cost air travel during the 1990s made the plans commercially unviable against the cheaper and quicker airlines.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Other reasons that have been suggested for these services having never been run were both government policies and the disruptive <a href="/wiki/Privatisation_of_British_Rail" title="Privatisation of British Rail">privatisation of British Rail</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-regionfail_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-regionfail-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Three of the Regional Eurostar units were leased by <a href="/wiki/Great_North_Eastern_Railway" title="Great North Eastern Railway">Great North Eastern Railway</a> (GNER) to increase domestic services from <a href="/wiki/London_King%27s_Cross_railway_station" title="London King&#39;s Cross railway station">London King\'s Cross</a> to York and later Leeds.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> The lease expired in December 2005, and most of the NoL sets were transferred to <a href="/wiki/SNCF" title="SNCF">SNCF</a> for <a href="/wiki/TGV" title="TGV">TGV</a> services in northern France.<sup id="cite_ref-CTRLrailtec_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CTRLrailtec-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>An international <a href="/wiki/Nightstar_(train)" title="Nightstar (train)">Nightstar</a> sleeper train was also planned; this would have travelled the same routes as Regional Eurostar, plus the <a href="/wiki/Great_Western_Main_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Western Main Line">Great Western Main Line</a> to <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_Central_railway_station" title="Cardiff Central railway station">Cardiff Central</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> These were also deemed commercially unviable, and the scheme was abandoned with no services ever operated. In 2000, the coaches were sold to <a href="/wiki/Via_Rail" title="Via Rail">Via Rail</a> in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ashford_International_station">Ashford International station</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Ashford International station">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ashford_International_Station_01.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Ashford_International_Station_01.JPG/220px-Ashford_International_Station_01.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Ashford_International_Station_01.JPG/330px-Ashford_International_Station_01.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Ashford_International_Station_01.JPG/440px-Ashford_International_Station_01.JPG 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ashford_International_Station_01.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Domestic entrance to <a href="/wiki/Ashford_International" class="mw-redirect" title="Ashford International">Ashford International</a>, since 2007</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ashford_International_railway_station" title="Ashford International railway station">Ashford International railway station</a></div>\n<p>Ashford International station was the original station for Eurostar services in <a href="/wiki/Kent" title="Kent">Kent</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\nOnce Ebbsfleet International railway station, also designed to serve Kent, had opened, only three trains a day to Paris Nord and one to Disneyland Paris called at Ashford for a considerable period of time. There were fears that services at Ashford International might be further reduced or withdrawn altogether as Eurostar planned to make Ebbsfleet the new regional hub instead.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> However, after a period during which no Brussels trains served the station,<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> to the dissatisfaction of the local communities,<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Eurostar reintroduced a single daily Ashford\xe2\x80\x93Brussels service on 23 February 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Changes_to_corporate_structure">Changes to corporate structure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Changes to corporate structure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 1 September 2010, Eurostar was incorporated as a single corporate entity, <a href="/wiki/Eurostar_International_Limited" title="Eurostar International Limited">Eurostar International Limited</a> (EIL), replacing the joint operation between EUKL, SNCF and SNCB/NMBS.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> EIL is owned by <a href="/wiki/SNCF" title="SNCF">SNCF</a> (55%), <a href="/wiki/Caisse_de_d%C3%A9p%C3%B4t_et_placement_du_Qu%C3%A9bec" title="Caisse de d\xc3\xa9p\xc3\xb4t et placement du Qu\xc3\xa9bec">Caisse de d\xc3\xa9p\xc3\xb4t et placement du Qu\xc3\xa9bec</a> (CDPQ) (30%), <a href="/wiki/Hermes_Infrastructure" class="mw-redirect" title="Hermes Infrastructure">Hermes Infrastructure</a> (10%) and <a href="/wiki/NMBS/SNCB" class="mw-redirect" title="NMBS/SNCB">SNCB</a> (5%).<sup id="cite_ref-bbc-20150304-sale_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-20150304-sale-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-eurostar.com_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eurostar.com-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-realestate.ipe.com_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-realestate.ipe.com-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In June 2014, the UK shareholding in Eurostar International Limited was transferred from London and Continental Railways / <a href="/wiki/Department_for_Transport" title="Department for Transport">Department for Transport</a> to <a href="/wiki/HM_Treasury" title="HM Treasury">HM Treasury</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> That October, it was announced that the UK government planned to raise \xc2\xa3300 million by selling its stake.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> In March 2015, the UK government announced that it would sell its 40% share to an Anglo-Canadian consortium made up of the Caisse and Hermes Infrastructure. The sale was completed in May 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-eurostar.com_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eurostar.com-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rules_for_cycles_on_trains">Rules for cycles on trains</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Rules for cycles on trains">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 2015, Eurostar threatened to require that cyclists dismantle bicycles before they could be transported on the trains. Following criticism from <a href="/wiki/Boris_Johnson" title="Boris Johnson">Boris Johnson</a> and cycling groups, Eurostar reversed the plans.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wi-Fi_and_onboard_entertainment">Wi-Fi and onboard entertainment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Wi-Fi and onboard entertainment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>By March 2016, onboard entertainment was provided by <a href="/wiki/GoMedia" title="GoMedia">GoMedia</a>, including Wi-Fi connectivity and up to 300 hours of movies and television kept on the train\'s servers and accessed using the passenger\'s own devices: mobile phones, tablets, laptops etc. A tracker app allows customers to see where they are.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Merger_with_Thalys">Merger with Thalys</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Merger with Thalys">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 27 September 2019, the heads of two of Eurostar\'s major shareholders, <a href="/wiki/Guillaume_Pepy" title="Guillaume Pepy">Guillaume Pepy</a> of SNCF, and the chair of SNCB <a href="/w/index.php?title=Sophie_Dutordoir&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Sophie Dutordoir (page does not exist)">Sophie Dutordoir</a><sup class="noprint" style="font-style: normal;">&#160;&#91;<a href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sophie_Dutordoir" class="extiw" title="fr:Sophie Dutordoir">fr</a>; <a href="https://nl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sophie_Dutordoir" class="extiw" title="nl:Sophie Dutordoir">nl</a>&#93;</sup>, publicised that Eurostar was planning to come together with its sister company the Franco-Belgian transnational rail service <a href="/wiki/Thalys" title="Thalys">Thalys</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> The arrangement is to merge their operations under the working title of "<i>Green Speed</i>" and expand services outside the core London-Paris-Brussels-Amsterdam service, to create a grand Western European high-speed rail service covering the UK, France, Belgium, the Netherlands and Germany, serving up to 30 million customers by 2030.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As of 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, Thalys assisted Eurostar with onwards connections between Amsterdam and Brussels, and to provide the Amsterdam to London service, in lieu of passport and customs checks at <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Centraal_station" title="Amsterdam Centraal station">Amsterdam Centraal station</a>. Thalys currently uses two ex-Eurostar <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_373" title="British Rail Class 373">class 373</a> trains (half-sets 373213 and 373224) to provide Thalys\' no frills service <a href="/wiki/IZY" title="IZY">IZY</a>, between Paris and Brussels.\n</p><p>In September 2020, the merger between Thalys and Eurostar International was confirmed,<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> a year after Thalys announced its intention to merge with the cross-Channel provider subject to gaining <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a> clearance, to form "Green Speed". SNCF and SNCB already hold a controlling shareholding in Eurostar.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="COVID-19_Impact">COVID-19 Impact</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: COVID-19 Impact">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>By January 2021, Eurostar ridership went down to less than 1% of pre-pandemic levels.<sup id="cite_ref-travelleisure_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-travelleisure-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> The combined financial troubles and lack of ridership caused by the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a> led to Eurostar seeking governmental assistance from <a href="/wiki/HM_Treasury" title="HM Treasury">Britain\'s Treasury</a> and <a href="/wiki/Department_for_Transport" title="Department for Transport">Department for Transport</a>, even though Britain sold its 40% Eurostar holding in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-travelleisure_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-travelleisure-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-rficollapse_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rficollapse-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bloomberglobby_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bloomberglobby-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> Eurostar\'s appeal included granting the company access to <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_England" title="Bank of England">Bank of England</a>-backed loans and a temporary reduction in track access charges for use of the UK\'s high-speed rail line.<sup id="cite_ref-travelleisure_51-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-travelleisure-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> Despite being majority-owned by the French state railway, <a href="/wiki/SNCF" title="SNCF">SNCF</a>, Eurostar was thought to have already exhausted options for governmental assistance from Paris,<sup id="cite_ref-guardianwarns_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardianwarns-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> but both the French transport minister and the UK Department for Transport confirmed they were working on further plans to maintain the service.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Mainline_routes">Mainline routes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Mainline routes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Networks_of_Major_High_Speed_Rail_Operators_in_Europe.gif" class="image"><img alt="" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Networks_of_Major_High_Speed_Rail_Operators_in_Europe.gif/330px-Networks_of_Major_High_Speed_Rail_Operators_in_Europe.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Networks_of_Major_High_Speed_Rail_Operators_in_Europe.gif/440px-Networks_of_Major_High_Speed_Rail_Operators_in_Europe.gif 2x" data-file-width="1980" data-file-height="1316" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Networks_of_Major_High_Speed_Rail_Operators_in_Europe.gif" class="internal"
