srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/BSicon_KHSTe.svg/30px-BSicon_KHSTe.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/BSicon_KHSTe.svg/40px-BSicon_KHSTe.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="500" /></div>\n</td>\n<td class="RMr1"><div class="RMsi">7:51</div>\n</td>\n<td class="RMr"><a href="/wiki/Bourg-Saint-Maurice_station" title="Bourg-Saint-Maurice station">Bourg-Saint-Maurice</a>\n</td>\n<td class="RMr4"><div class="RMsi"><a href="/wiki/SNCF" title="SNCF"><img alt="SNCF" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/SNCF_no_text.png/15px-SNCF_no_text.png" decoding="async" width="15" height="8" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/SNCF_no_text.png/23px-SNCF_no_text.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/SNCF_no_text.png/30px-SNCF_no_text.png 2x" data-file-width="119" data-file-height="62" /></a></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="padding:0 3px 0 0;">\n</td>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td class="RMl1">\n</td>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td class="RMr1">\n</td>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td style="padding:0 0 0 3px;">\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="line-height:normal;text-align:right;padding:0px 5px 5px;"><div class="center" style="width:auto; margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;"><i>Fastest timetabled journeys<br />from London St Pancras</i></div>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span id="LGV_Nord_.28France.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="LGV_Nord_(France)">LGV Nord (France)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: LGV Nord (France)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/LGV_Nord" title="LGV Nord">LGV Nord</a></div>\n<p>LGV Nord is a French 333-kilometre (207&#160;mi)-long <a href="/wiki/High-speed_rail" title="High-speed rail">high-speed rail</a> line that connects Paris to the Belgian border and the Channel Tunnel via <a href="/wiki/Lille" title="Lille">Lille</a>. It opened in 1993.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>\nIts extensions to Belgium and towards Paris, as well as connecting to the Channel Tunnel, have made LGV Nord a part of every Eurostar journey undertaken. A Belgian high-speed line, HSL 1, was added to the end of LGV Nord, at the Belgian border, in 1997. Of all French high-speed lines, LGV Nord sees the widest variety of high-speed rolling stock and is quite busy; a proposed cut-off bypassing Lille, which would reduce Eurostar journey times to Paris, is called <a href="/wiki/LGV_Picardie" title="LGV Picardie">LGV Picardie</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Channel_Tunnel">Channel Tunnel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Channel Tunnel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Channel_Tunnel" title="Channel Tunnel">Channel Tunnel</a></div>\n<p>The Channel Tunnel is the most important part of the route as it is the only rail connection between Great Britain and the European mainland. It joins LGV Nord in France with High Speed One in Britain. Tunnelling began in 1988, and the 50.5-kilometre (31.4&#160;mi) tunnel was officially opened by British sovereign <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II_of_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Elizabeth II of the United Kingdom">Queen Elizabeth II</a> and the French President <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Mitterrand" title="Fran\xc3\xa7ois Mitterrand">Fran\xc3\xa7ois Mitterrand</a> at a ceremony in Calais on 6 May 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_openingceremony_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_openingceremony-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>\nIt is owned by <a href="/wiki/Getlink" title="Getlink">Getlink</a>, which charges a significant toll to Eurostar for its use.<sup id="cite_ref-Eurotoll_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eurotoll-59">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>\nIn 1996, the <a href="/wiki/American_Society_of_Civil_Engineers" title="American Society of Civil Engineers">American Society of Civil Engineers</a> named the tunnel as one of the <a href="/wiki/Wonders_of_the_World#American_Society_of_Civil_Engineers" title="Wonders of the World">Seven Wonders of the Modern World</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Plain_Dealer_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Plain_Dealer-60">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>\nAlong the current route of the Eurostar service, line speeds are 300 kilometres per hour (186&#160;mph) except within the Channel Tunnel, where a reduced speed of 160 kilometres per hour (100&#160;mph) applies for safety reasons.<sup id="cite_ref-railfaneurostar_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-railfaneurostar-61">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-eurotunnrules_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eurotunnrules-62">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\nSince the launch of Eurostar services, severe disruptions and cancellations have been caused by fires breaking out within the Channel Tunnel, such as in <a href="/wiki/1996_Channel_Tunnel_fire" title="1996 Channel Tunnel fire">1996</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Kirkland_fire_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kirkland_fire-63">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Channel_Tunnel#Fires" title="Channel Tunnel">2006</a> (minor),<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_fire_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_fire-64">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/2008_Channel_Tunnel_fire" title="2008 Channel Tunnel fire">2008</a> and 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-Tunnelfire_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tunnelfire-65">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="HSL_1_.28Belgium.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="HSL_1_(Belgium)">HSL 1 (Belgium)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: HSL 1 (Belgium)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/HSL_1" title="HSL 1">HSL 1</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eurostar_by_Silly.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Eurostar_by_Silly.jpg/220px-Eurostar_by_Silly.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Eurostar_by_Silly.jpg/330px-Eurostar_by_Silly.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Eurostar_by_Silly.jpg/440px-Eurostar_by_Silly.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eurostar_by_Silly.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Eurostar train on HSL 1 near <a href="/wiki/Silly,_Belgium" title="Silly, Belgium">Silly, Belgium</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Until the opening on 2 June 1996, of the first phase of the Belgian high speed line,<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> Eurostar trains were routed via the <a href="/wiki/Belgian_railway_line_94" title="Belgian railway line 94">Belgian railway line 94</a>. The Eurostar routes still use the line as a diversion if engineering works are taking place on HSL1, depending where it is. The 06:13 from London St Pancras to Brussels still uses the line as a diversion to bypass the peak time disruptions on HSL1 due to the extra TGV services from Brussels for the commuters. After 2 June 1996, some Eurostars to Brussels were routed via the first phase of the Belgian High Speed line and the Belgian railway line 78 via <a href="/wiki/Mons" title="Mons">Mons</a>. Although this line is still as a diversion if HSL1 is doing engineering, also depending where the maintenance is taking place.<sup id="cite_ref-Rail_Chronology:_Eurostar_services_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rail_Chronology:_Eurostar_services-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Journey times between London and Brussels were improved when an 88-kilometre (55&#160;mi) Belgian high-speed line, <a href="/wiki/HSL_1" title="HSL 1">HSL 1</a>, opened on 14 December 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> It links with LGV Nord on the border with France, allowing Eurostar trains heading to Brussels to make the transition between the two without having to reduce speed. A further four-minute improvement for London\xe2\x80\x93Brussels trains was achieved in December 2006, with the opening of the 435-metre (1,427&#160;ft) Brussels South Viaduct.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> Linking the international platforms of Brussels-South railway station with the high-speed line, the viaduct separates Eurostar (and Thalys) from local services.\n</p>\n<div style="clear:left;"></div>\n<h3><span id="High_Speed_1_.28United_Kingdom.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="High_Speed_1_(United_Kingdom)">High Speed 1 (United Kingdom)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: High Speed 1 (United Kingdom)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/High_Speed_1" title="High Speed 1">High Speed 1</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:StroodCTRL2.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/StroodCTRL2.JPG/220px-StroodCTRL2.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/StroodCTRL2.JPG/330px-StroodCTRL2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/StroodCTRL2.JPG/440px-StroodCTRL2.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2016" data-file-height="1512" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:StroodCTRL2.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Eurostar train on High Speed 1 near <a href="/wiki/Strood" title="Strood">Strood</a>, South East England</div></div></div>\n<p>High Speed 1 (HS1), formerly known as the Channel Tunnel Rail Link (CTRL), is a 108-kilometre (67&#160;mi) high-speed railway line running from London through <a href="/wiki/Kent" title="Kent">Kent</a> to the British end of the Channel Tunnel.<sup id="cite_ref-railtechhs10_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-railtechhs10-70">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>\nIt was built in two stages. The first section between the tunnel and <a href="/wiki/Fawkham_Junction" title="Fawkham Junction">Fawkham Junction</a> in north Kent opened in September 2003, cutting London\xe2\x80\x93Paris journey times by 21&#160;minutes to 2&#160;hours 35&#160;minutes, and London\xe2\x80\x93Brussels to 2&#160;hours 20&#160;minutes. On 14 November 2007, commercial services began over the whole of the new HS1 line. The redeveloped St Pancras International station became the new London <a href="/wiki/Terminal_train_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Terminal train station">terminus</a> for all Eurostar services.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc20071114_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc20071114-72">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>\nThe completion of High Speed 1 has brought the British part of Eurostar\'s route up to the same standards as the French and Belgian high-speed lines. Non-stop journey times were reduced by a further 20&#160;minutes to 2&#160;hours 15&#160;minutes for London\xe2\x80\x93Paris and 1&#160;hour 51&#160;minutes for London\xe2\x80\x93Brussels.<sup id="cite_ref-alstomhs1_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alstomhs1-73">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> As of fall 2020, HS1 is the UK\'s first renewable-powered railway.<sup id="cite_ref-hs1green_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hs1green-75">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Services">Services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Frequency">Frequency</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Frequency">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eurostar_departure_information_-_Brussels.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Eurostar_departure_information_-_Brussels.JPG/220px-Eurostar_departure_information_-_Brussels.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Eurostar_departure_information_-_Brussels.JPG/330px-Eurostar_departure_information_-_Brussels.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Eurostar_departure_information_-_Brussels.JPG/440px-Eurostar_departure_information_-_Brussels.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eurostar_departure_information_-_Brussels.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Eurostar departure information \xe2\x80\x93 Brussels</div></div></div>\n<p>Eurostar offers up to fifteen weekday London \xe2\x80\x93 Paris services (nineteen on Fridays) including nine non-stop (thirteen on Fridays). There are also nine (ten on Friday) London\xe2\x80\x93Brussels services, with two running non-stop (continuing to Amsterdam) and a further two calling at Lille only. One service daily operates to Amsterdam via Brussels and Rotterdam also calling at Lille.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> In addition, there is a return trip from London to <a href="/wiki/Gare_de_Marne-la-Vall%C3%A9e_-_Chessy" class="mw-redirect" title="Gare de Marne-la-Vall\xc3\xa9e - Chessy">Marne-la-Vall\xc3\xa9e - Chessy</a> for <a href="/wiki/Disneyland_Resort_Paris" class="mw-redirect" title="Disneyland Resort Paris">Disneyland Paris</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> which runs 4 times a week with increased frequency during school holidays. There are also seasonal services: an up-to-4-times-a-week service to Marseille via Lyon and Avignon in the summer; and, in the winter, "Snow trains",<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> aimed at skiers, to <a href="/wiki/Bourg-Saint-Maurice" title="Bourg-Saint-Maurice">Bourg-Saint-Maurice</a>, <a href="/wiki/La_Plagne" title="La Plagne">Aime-la-Plagne</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mo%C3%BBtiers" title="Mo\xc3\xbbtiers">Mo\xc3\xbbtiers</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Alps" title="Alps">Alps</a>; these run twice-weekly, one overnight and one during the daytime.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> Intermediate stations are Ebbsfleet International in northwest Kent, Ashford International in southeast Kent, and <a href="/wiki/Gare_de_Calais-Fr%C3%A9thun" class="mw-redirect" title="Gare de Calais-Fr\xc3\xa9thun">Calais-Fr\xc3\xa9thun</a> and Lille-Europe in Nord-Pas-de-Calais.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> In February 2018, Eurostar announced the start of its long planned service from London to Amsterdam, with an initial two trains per day from April of that year running between St Pancras and <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Centraal_station" title="Amsterdam Centraal station">Amsterdam Centraal</a>. This launched as a one-way service, with return trains carrying passengers to Rotterdam and Brussels Midi/Zuid, making a 28-minute stop (which has not been deemed long enough to process UK-bound passengers) and then carrying different passengers from Brussels to London.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> Initially passengers travelling back took a <a href="/wiki/Thalys" title="Thalys">Thalys</a> services to Brussels Midi/Zuid where they could join the Eurostar. This was is due to the lack of facilities for <a href="/wiki/Juxtaposed_controls" title="Juxtaposed controls">juxtaposed controls</a> by the <a href="/wiki/UK_Border_Force" class="mw-redirect" title="UK Border Force">UK Border Force</a> at Amsterdam Centraal and Rotterdam Centraal. On 4 February 2020, the Dutch <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Infrastructure_and_Water_Management" title="Ministry of Infrastructure and Water Management">Minister of Infrastructure and Water Management</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cora_van_Nieuwenhuizen" title="Cora van Nieuwenhuizen">Cora van Nieuwenhuizen</a>, and the UK <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_Transport" title="Secretary of State for Transport">Transport Secretary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grant_Shapps" title="Grant Shapps">Grant Shapps</a>, announced that <a href="/wiki/Juxtaposed_controls" title="Juxtaposed controls">juxtaposed controls</a> would be established at Amsterdam Centraal and Rotterdam Centraal. The direct train from Amsterdam was originally due to launch on 30 April 2020, and from Rotterdam on 18 May 2020,<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> although it was later postponed to 26 October 2020 for both cities due to the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Since 14 November 2007, all Eurostar trains have been routed via High Speed&#160;1 to or from the redeveloped London terminus at St Pancras International, which at a cost of \xc2\xa3800&#160;million was extensively rebuilt and extended to cope with 394-metre (431&#160;yd) long Eurostar trains.<sup id="cite_ref-transpancras_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-transpancras-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>\nIt had been intended to retain some Eurostar services at <a href="/wiki/Waterloo_International_railway_station" title="Waterloo International railway station">Waterloo International</a>, but this was ruled out on cost grounds.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>\nCompletion of High Speed&#160;1 has increased the potential number of trains serving London. Separation of Eurostar from British domestic services through Kent meant that timetabling was no longer affected by peak-hour restrictions.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fares">Fares</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Fares">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eurostar_at_St_Pancras_Jan_2008.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Eurostar_at_St_Pancras_Jan_2008.jpg/220px-Eurostar_at_St_Pancras_Jan_2008.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="175" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Eurostar_at_St_Pancras_Jan_2008.jpg/330px-Eurostar_at_St_Pancras_Jan_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Eurostar_at_St_Pancras_Jan_2008.jpg/440px-Eurostar_at_St_Pancras_Jan_2008.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2380" data-file-height="1889" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eurostar_at_St_Pancras_Jan_2008.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Eurostar trains in the renovated train shed at <a href="/wiki/St_Pancras_International_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="St Pancras International railway station">St Pancras International</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Eurostar\'s fares were significantly higher in its early years; the cheapest fare in 1994 was \xc2\xa399 return.<sup id="cite_ref-savtrav_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-savtrav-90">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>\nIn 2002, Eurostar was planning cheaper fares, an example of which was an offer of \xc2\xa350-day returns from London to Paris or Brussels. \nBy March 2003, the cheapest fare from the UK was \xc2\xa359 return, available all year around.<sup id="cite_ref-savtrav_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-savtrav-90">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> In June 2009 it was announced that one-way single fares would be available at \xc2\xa331 at the cheapest. Competition between Eurostar and airline services was a large factor in ticket prices being reduced from the initial levels.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>\nBusiness Premier fares also slightly undercut air fares on similar routes, targeted at regular business travellers.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>\nIn 2009, Eurostar greatly increased its budget ticket availability to help maintain and grow its dominant market share.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> \nThe Eurostar ticketing system is very complex, being distributed through no fewer than 48 individual sales systems.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>\nEurostar is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Amadeus_CRS" title="Amadeus CRS">Amadeus CRS</a> distribution system, making its tickets available alongside those of airlines worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/First_class_travel" title="First class travel">First class</a> on Eurostar is called Business Premier; benefits include guaranteed faster checking-in and meals served at-seat, as well as the improved furnishings and interior of Business Premier carriages.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>\nThe rebranding is part of Eurostar\'s marketing drive to attract more business professionals.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> Increasingly, business people in a group have been chartering private carriages as opposed to individual seats on the train.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Service_connections">Service connections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Service connections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eurostar_Thalys_and_TGV.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/86/Eurostar_Thalys_and_TGV.JPG/220px-Eurostar_Thalys_and_TGV.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/86/Eurostar_Thalys_and_TGV.JPG/330px-Eurostar_Thalys_and_TGV.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/86/Eurostar_Thalys_and_TGV.JPG/440px-Eurostar_Thalys_and_TGV.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eurostar_Thalys_and_TGV.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Two Eurostar trains, a <a href="/wiki/Thalys" title="Thalys">Thalys</a> train, and a <a href="/wiki/TGV" title="TGV">TGV</a> train side by side at Paris <a href="/wiki/Gare_du_Nord" title="Gare du Nord">Gare du Nord</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lille_Europe_Quai.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Lille_Europe_Quai.jpg/220px-Lille_Europe_Quai.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Lille_Europe_Quai.jpg/330px-Lille_Europe_Quai.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Lille_Europe_Quai.jpg/440px-Lille_Europe_Quai.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="375" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lille_Europe_Quai.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Gare de Lille-Europe in France, a common calling point for Eurostar and other TGV services</div></div></div>\n<p>Without the operation of <a href="/wiki/Regional_Eurostar" title="Regional Eurostar">Regional Eurostar</a> services using the North of London trainsets across the rest of Britain, Eurostar has developed its connections with other transport services instead, such as integrating effectively with traditional UK rail operators\' schedules and routes, making it possible for passengers to use Eurostar as a quick connection to further destinations on the continent.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>\nAll three main terminals used by the Eurostar service \xe2\x80\x93 St Pancras International, Paris Gare du Nord, and Brussels Midi/Zuid \xe2\x80\x93 are served by domestic trains and by local urban transport networks such as the <a href="/wiki/London_Underground" title="London Underground">London Underground</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Paris_Metro" class="mw-redirect" title="Paris Metro">Paris Metro</a>. Standard Eurostar tickets no longer include free onward connections to or from any other station in Belgium: this is now available for a flat-rate supplement, currently \xc2\xa35.50.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Eurostar has announced several partnerships with other rail services,<sup id="cite_ref-bahneuroally_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bahneuroally-101">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>\nmost notably <a href="/wiki/Thalys" title="Thalys">Thalys</a> connections at Lille and Brussels for passengers to go beyond current Eurostar routes towards the Netherlands and Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-ThalesEuro_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ThalesEuro-102">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>\nIn 2002, Eurostar initiated the Eurostar-Plus program, offering connecting tickets for onward journeys from Lille and Paris to dozens of destinations in France. \nThrough fares are also available from 68 British towns and cities to destinations in France and Belgium.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>\nIn May 2009 Eurostar announced that a formal connection to Switzerland had been established in a partnership between Eurostar and <a href="/wiki/TGV_Lyria" title="TGV Lyria">Lyria</a>, which will operate TGV services from Lille to the Swiss Alps for Eurostar connection.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In May 2019, Eurostar ended its agreement with Deutsche Bahn that allowed passengers to travel by train from the UK to Germany, Austria and Switzerland. Under the agreement passengers could travel on a single booking which made rescheduling easier. However, the direct tickets will no longer be sold from 9 November 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Controls_and_security">Controls and security</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Controls and security">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:308px;max-width:308px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:152px;max-width:152px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Uk_paris_entry.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A UK passport stamp issued in Paris" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Uk_paris_entry.jpg/150px-Uk_paris_entry.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="158" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Uk_paris_entry.jpg/225px-Uk_paris_entry.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Uk_paris_entry.jpg/300px-Uk_paris_entry.jpg 2x" data-file-width="372" data-file-height="391" /></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:152px;max-width:152px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:France_london_entry.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A Schengen (French) passport stamp issued in London" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/France_london_entry.jpg/150px-France_london_entry.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="110" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/France_london_entry.jpg/225px-France_london_entry.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/France_london_entry.jpg/300px-France_london_entry.jpg 2x" data-file-width="404" data-file-height="297" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption">Entering the UK in Paris (left) and France in London using the Eurostar.</div></div></div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Juxtaposed_controls" title="Juxtaposed controls">Juxtaposed controls</a></div>\n<p>Because the UK is not part of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> or the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Schengen_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schengen-108">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> and because the Netherlands, Belgium and France are not part of the <a href="/wiki/Common_Travel_Area" title="Common Travel Area">Common Travel Area</a>, all Eurostar passengers must go through border controls. Both the British Government and the Schengen governments concerned (Belgium, Netherlands and France) have legal obligations to check the travel documents of those entering and leaving their respective countries.\n</p><p>To allow passengers to walk off the train without arrival checks in most cases, <a href="/wiki/Juxtaposed_controls" title="Juxtaposed controls">juxtaposed controls</a> ordinarily take place at the embarkation station.\n</p><p>To comply with UK law,<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> there are full security checks similar to those at airports, scanning both bags and people\'s pockets. Security checks at Eurostar are comparable to those at a small airport and generally much quicker than at London Heathrow.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> The recommended check-in time is 30 minutes except for business class where it is 10 minutes.\n</p><p>Eurostar passengers travelling within the Schengen Area (Brussels\xe2\x80\x93Lille and Brussels\xe2\x80\x93Calais; Lille\xe2\x80\x93Calais trips are not allowed by Eurostar) pass through a separate corridor in Brussels bypassing border checks, and enter the preallocated cars of the train, which are reserved for these passengers. This arrangement was set up after numerous people entered the UK without prior authorisation, by buying a ticket from Brussels to Lille or Calais but remaining on the train until London \xe2\x80\x93 an issue exacerbated by Belgian police threatening to arrest UK Border Agency staff at Brussels-Midi if they tried to prevent passengers whom they suspected of attempting to exploit this loophole from boarding Eurostar trains.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> Travel from Calais or Lille towards Brussels has no border or security control. On the 7 July 2020 a modified agreement was signed in Brussels that includes The Netherlands in the previous agreement. This allows for juxtaposed controls in Amsterdam and Rotterdam like those in Brussels or Paris.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>When the tripartite agreements were signed, the <a href="/wiki/Belgian_federal_government" class="mw-redirect" title="Belgian federal government">Belgian Government</a> said that it had serious questions about the compatibility of this agreement with the Schengen Convention and the principle of free movement of people enshrined in various European treaties.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>\nOn 30 June 2009 Eurostar raised concerns at the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Commons_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="House of Commons of the United Kingdom">UK House of Commons</a> Home Affairs Select Committee that it was illegal under French law to collect the information required by the UK government under the <a href="/wiki/Border_control" title="Border control">e-Borders</a> scheme, and they would be unable to cooperate.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On the northbound Marne la Vall\xc3\xa9e-Chessy - London train, the security check and French passport check take place at Marne la Vall\xc3\xa9e-Chessy, while the UK passport check takes place at the UK arrival stations - this is the only route where passengers are not cleared by UK border officials before crossing the Channel.\n</p><p>On the northbound Marseille-London train, there is no facility for security or passport checks at the southern French stations, so passengers must leave the train at Lille-Europe, taking all their belongings with them, and undergo security and border checks there before rejoining the train which waits at the station for just over an hour.<sup id="cite_ref-dowd-bbc-052015_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dowd-bbc-052015-116">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On several occasions, people have tried to stow away illegally on board the train,<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> sometimes in large groups,<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> trying to enter the UK; border monitoring and security is therefore extremely tight.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>\nEurostar claims to have good and well-funded security measures.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Operational_performance">Operational performance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Operational performance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eurostar_Lille_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Eurostar_Lille_2.jpg/220px-Eurostar_Lille_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Eurostar_Lille_2.jpg/330px-Eurostar_Lille_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Eurostar_Lille_2.jpg/440px-Eurostar_Lille_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="816" data-file-height="616" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eurostar_Lille_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Eurostar pulling into <a href="/wiki/Gare_de_Lille-Europe" class="mw-redirect" title="Gare de Lille-Europe">Gare de Lille-Europe</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eurostar_market_shares.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Eurostar_market_shares.svg/220px-Eurostar_market_shares.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="125" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Eurostar_market_shares.svg/330px-Eurostar_market_shares.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Eurostar_market_shares.svg/440px-Eurostar_market_shares.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="577" data-file-height="328" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eurostar_market_shares.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Eurostar market share and punctuality.</div></div></div>\n<p>Eurostar\'s punctuality has fluctuated from year to year, but usually remains over 90%;<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> in the first quarter of 1999, 89% of services operated were on time, and in the second quarter it reached 92%.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> Eurostar\'s best punctuality record was 97.35%, between 16 and 22 August 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-Eurost_His_4-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eurost_His-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> In 2006, it was 92.7%,<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> and in 2007, 91.5% were on time.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> In the first quarter of 2009, 96% of Eurostar services were punctual, compared with rival air routes\' 76%.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>An advantage held by Eurostar is the convenience and speed of the service: with shorter check-in times than at most airports and hence quicker boarding and less queueing<sup id="cite_ref-secur_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-secur-127">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> and high punctuality, it takes less time to travel between central London and central Paris by high-speed rail than by air. Eurostar now has a dominant share of the combined rail\xe2\x80\x93air market on its routes to Paris and Brussels. In 2004, it had a 66% share of the London\xe2\x80\x93Paris market, and a 59% share of the London\xe2\x80\x93Brussels market.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> In 2007, it achieved record market shares of 71% for London\xe2\x80\x93Paris and 65% for London\xe2\x80\x93Brussels routes.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Eurostar\'s passenger numbers initially failed to meet predictions. In 1996, <a href="/wiki/London_and_Continental_Railways" title="London and Continental Railways">London and Continental Railways</a> forecast that passenger numbers would reach 21.4&#160;million annually by 2004,<sup id="cite_ref-LCR_fore_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LCR_fore-131">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> but only 7.3&#160;million was achieved. 82 million passengers used Waterloo International Station from its opening in 1994 to its closure in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-waterloovid_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-waterloovid-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> 2008 was a record year for Eurostar, with a 10.3% rise in passenger use, which was attributed to the use of High Speed 1 and the move to St Pancras.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> The following year, Eurostar saw an 11.5% fall in passenger numbers<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> during the first three months of 2009, attributed to the <a href="/wiki/2008_Channel_Tunnel_fire" title="2008 Channel Tunnel fire">2008 Channel Tunnel fire</a><sup id="cite_ref-Tunnelfire_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tunnelfire-65">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/2009_recession" class="mw-redirect" title="2009 recession">2009 recession</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As a result of the poor economic conditions, Eurostar received state aid in May 2009 to cancel out some of the accumulated debt from the High Speed 1 construction programme.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> Later that year, during snowy conditions in the run-up to Christmas, thousands of passengers were left stranded as several trains broke down and many more were cancelled. In an independent review commissioned by Eurostar, the company came in for serious criticism about its handling of the incident and lack of plans for such a scenario.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2006, the <a href="/wiki/Department_for_Transport" title="Department for Transport">Department for Transport</a> predicted that, by 2037, annual cross-channel passenger numbers would probably reach 16 million,<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> considerably less optimistic than London and Continental Railways\'s original 1996 forecast.<sup id="cite_ref-LCR_fore_131-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LCR_fore-131">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> In 2007 Eurostar set a target of carrying 10&#160;million passengers by 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup>\nThe company cited several factors to support this objective, such as improved journey times, punctuality and station facilities. Passengers in general, it stated, are becoming increasingly aware of the environmental effects of air travel, and Eurostar services emit much less <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">carbon dioxide</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> and that its remaining carbon emissions are now <a href="/wiki/Carbon_offset" title="Carbon offset">offset</a>, making its services <a href="/wiki/Carbon_neutral" class="mw-redirect" title="Carbon neutral">carbon neutral</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> Further expansion of the high-speed rail network in Europe, such as the <a href="/wiki/HSL-Zuid" title="HSL-Zuid">HSL-Zuid</a> line between Belgium and the Netherlands, continues to bring more destinations within rail-competitive range, giving Eurostar the possibility of opening up new services in future.\n</p><p>The following chart presents the estimated number of passengers annually transported by the Eurostar service since 1995:\n<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1017906329">@media all and (max-width:720px){body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output mw-graph-nofallback" style="min-width:600px;min-height:250px" data-graph-id="d21955fc4a80eca081e83fd0cc6bcbdaf0061407"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_accolades">Awards and accolades</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Awards and accolades">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eurostar_trainsets_at_Paris_Nord.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eurostar_trainsets_at_Paris_Nord.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Several Eurostar trains at platforms at Paris Gare du Nord</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:DSC_7230-voies-de-la-gare-d.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/DSC_7230-voies-de-la-gare-d.jpg/220px-DSC_7230-voies-de-la-gare-d.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/DSC_7230-voies-de-la-gare-d.jpg/330px-DSC_7230-voies-de-la-gare-d.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/DSC_7230-voies-de-la-gare-d.jpg/440px-DSC_7230-voies-de-la-gare-d.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1504" data-file-height="1000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:DSC_7230-voies-de-la-gare-d.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Eurostars at Paris <a href="/wiki/Gare_du_Nord" title="Gare du Nord">Gare du Nord</a> running late night services</div></div></div>\n<p>Eurostar has been hailed as having set new standards in international rail travel and has won praise several times over for its high standards.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> However, Eurostar had previously struggled with its reputation and brand image. One commentator had defined the situation at the time as:<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>In June 2003, Eurostar was battling to recover from the worst period in its 10-year history. Negative media coverage combined with poor sales and the general public\'s low opinion of the British rail industry, created a major challenge... Eurostar was finding it difficult to pick itself up from one of the worst periods in its decade-long history. The period post <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">9/11</a> had sent the business into a downturn. Passenger numbers were drying up due to worries over international travel. Several management changes had led to a pause in strategy. Punctuality had suffered badly because of wider problems with the UK\'s rail infrastructure.</p></blockquote>\n<p>Eurostar won the <a href="/wiki/Train_Operator_of_the_Year" title="Train Operator of the Year">Train Operator of the Year</a> award in the <a href="/wiki/HSBC" title="HSBC">HSBC</a> Rail Awards for 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-bahneuroally_101-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bahneuroally-101">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> In 2006, Eurostar\'s Environment Group was set up,<sup id="cite_ref-greennetrail_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-greennetrail-154">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> with the aim of making changes in the Eurostar services\' daily running to decrease negative environmental impact.<sup id="cite_ref-greeneuro_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-greeneuro-155">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> The organization set itself a target of reducing carbon emissions per passenger journey by 25% by 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-greeneuro_155-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-greeneuro-155">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> Drivers were trained in techniques to achieve maximum energy efficiency, and lighting was minimised; the provider of the bulk of the energy for the Channel Tunnel was switched to nuclear power stations in France.<sup id="cite_ref-greeneuro_155-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-greeneuro-155">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> Eurostar\'s target was to reduce emissions by 35 percent per passenger journey by 2012, putting itself beyond the efforts of other railway companies in this field and thereby winning the 2007 <a href="/wiki/Network_Rail" title="Network Rail">Network Rail</a> Efficiency Award.<sup id="cite_ref-greennetrail_154-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-greennetrail-154">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> In the grand opening ceremony of St Pancras International, one of the Eurostar trains was given the name \'Tread Lightly\', said to symbolise their smaller impact on the environment compared to planes.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> By 2008, Eurostar\'s environmental credentials had become highly developed and promoted.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Since then, Eurostar has received multiple awards. It was declared the Best Train Company in the joint <a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">Guardian</a>/<a href="/wiki/The_Observer" title="The Observer">Observer</a> Travel Awards 2008<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> and earned a spot on the Sunday Times\' Best Green Companies List (2009).<sup id="cite_ref-sundaytimes_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sundaytimes-159">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> Other awards include: ICARUS\xe2\x80\x99 Environmental Award for Best Rail Provider (2009),<sup id="cite_ref-allenyork_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allenyork-160">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> Guardian &amp; Observer Travel Award for Best Train Company (2009),<sup id="cite_ref-guardianobserver_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardianobserver-161">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> Travel Weekly\'s Golden Globes Award for Best Rail Operator (2010),<sup id="cite_ref-travelgolden_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-travelgolden-162">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> World Travel Market\'s Responsible Tourism Award for Best Low Carbon Initiative (2011),<sup id="cite_ref-responsible_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-responsible-163">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> TNT Magazine\'s Gold Backpack Award for Favourite Travel Transport (2012),<sup id="cite_ref-tnt_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tnt-164">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> World Travel Awards Europe\'s Leading Passenger Rail Operator (2011),<sup id="cite_ref-worldtravellead_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worldtravellead-165">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> National Rail Awards Train of the Year (2017),<sup id="cite_ref-railmagazine_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-railmagazine-166">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> PETA\'s Travel Award for Best Travel Experience (2019),<sup id="cite_ref-mobile_2020_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mobile_2020-167">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> Mobile Industry Awards\' Distributor of the Year (2020).<sup id="cite_ref-petaaward_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-petaaward-168">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_Initiatives">Environmental Initiatives</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Environmental Initiatives">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 2007, Eurostar became the world\'s first carbon-neutral train service through its launch of \xe2\x80\x9cTread Lightly,\xe2\x80\x9d an environmental program with the goal of reducing the trainline\'s carbon dioxide emissions by 25% by 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-greenlight_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-greenlight-169">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-industryweekeco_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-industryweekeco-170">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> The program included: reducing power consumption on its rolling stock; sourcing more electricity from lower-emission generators; adding new controls on lighting, heating, and air conditioning; reducing paper usage via electronic tickets; recycling water and employee uniforms; sourcing all food on board from Britain, France, or Belgium.<sup id="cite_ref-industryweekeco_170-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-industryweekeco-170">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> Eurostar also funded three renewable energy projects in developing regions around the world: a windfarm in Tamil Nadu, India; a micro-hydropower project in China; a plan specifying improvements on fuel consumption of three-wheeler taxis in Indonesia.<sup id="cite_ref-greenlight_169-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-greenlight-169">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2019, Eurostar removed all single-use plastics from its trains between London and Paris.<sup id="cite_ref-globalrailwayrev_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-globalrailwayrev-171">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> Now the lines only serve wooden cutlery, recyclable cans of water, glass wine bottles, paper-based coffee cups, and eco-friendly food packaging.<sup id="cite_ref-globalrailwayrev_171-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-globalrailwayrev-171">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-businesseco_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-businesseco-172">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-lonelyplanet_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lonelyplanet-173">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> Eurostar partnered with the Woodland Trust, ReforestAction, and Trees for All in 2020, with the goal of planting 20,000 trees each year in woodlands along its routes across the UK, Belgium, and the Netherlands. Since Tread Lightly launched, Eurostar has reduced its carbon footprint by over 40% and now emits up to 90% less greenhouse gas emissions than the equivalent flight.<sup id="cite_ref-globalrailwayrev_171-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-globalrailwayrev-171">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-businesseco_172-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-businesseco-172">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-lonelyplanet_173-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lonelyplanet-173">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Organisation">Organisation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Organisation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Eurostar_International_Limited" title="Eurostar International Limited">Eurostar International Limited</a></div>\n<p>Since 2010, Eurostar has been owned by Eurostar International Limited (EIL), a company jointly owned by <a href="/wiki/SNCF" title="SNCF">SNCF</a> (55%), <i lang="fr" title="French-language text"><a href="/wiki/Caisse_de_d%C3%A9p%C3%B4t_et_placement_du_Qu%C3%A9bec" title="Caisse de d\xc3\xa9p\xc3\xb4t et placement du Qu\xc3\xa9bec">Caisse de d\xc3\xa9p\xc3\xb4t et placement du Qu\xc3\xa9bec</a></i> (CDPQ) (30%), <a href="/wiki/Hermes_Infrastructure" class="mw-redirect" title="Hermes Infrastructure">Hermes Infrastructure</a> (10%) and <a href="/wiki/SNCB" class="mw-redirect" title="SNCB">SNCB</a> (5%).<sup id="cite_ref-realestate.ipe.com_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-realestate.ipe.com-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Railteam">Railteam</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Railteam">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Eurostar is a member of <a href="/wiki/Railteam" title="Railteam">Railteam</a>, a marketing alliance formed in July 2007 of seven European <a href="/wiki/High-speed_rail" title="High-speed rail">high-speed rail</a> operators.<sup id="cite_ref-highspeedrev_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-highspeedrev-174">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup>\nThe alliance plans to allow tickets to be booked from one end of Europe to the other on a single website.<sup id="cite_ref-highspeedrev_174-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-highspeedrev-174">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> In June 2009 London and Continental Railways, and the Eurostar UK operations they held ownership of, became fully <a href="/wiki/Nationalised" class="mw-redirect" title="Nationalised">nationalised</a> by the UK government.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Fleet">Fleet</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Fleet">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline"
