/></a>\n</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<p>In addition to its multiple unit fleet units, Eurostar operates a single <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_08" title="British Rail Class 08">Class 08</a> diesel shunter as the pilot at <a href="/wiki/Temple_Mills" title="Temple Mills">Temple Mills depot</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_fleet">Current fleet</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Current fleet">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Class_373">Class 373</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Class 373">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rame_Eurostar_en_Savoie.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Rame_Eurostar_en_Savoie.JPG/220px-Rame_Eurostar_en_Savoie.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Rame_Eurostar_en_Savoie.JPG/330px-Rame_Eurostar_en_Savoie.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Rame_Eurostar_en_Savoie.JPG/440px-Rame_Eurostar_en_Savoie.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1984" data-file-height="1488" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rame_Eurostar_en_Savoie.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Eurostar in <a href="/wiki/Savoie" title="Savoie">Savoie</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/French_Alps" title="French Alps">French Alps</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eurostar_trains_at_St_Pancras.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Eurostar_trains_at_St_Pancras.jpg/220px-Eurostar_trains_at_St_Pancras.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Eurostar_trains_at_St_Pancras.jpg/330px-Eurostar_trains_at_St_Pancras.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Eurostar_trains_at_St_Pancras.jpg/440px-Eurostar_trains_at_St_Pancras.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eurostar_trains_at_St_Pancras.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Three Eurostar trains waiting at <a href="/wiki/St_Pancras_railway_station" title="St Pancras railway station">St Pancras station</a></div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_373" title="British Rail Class 373">British Rail Class 373</a></div>\n<p>Built between 1992 and 1996, Eurostar\'s fleet consists of 38 <a href="/wiki/Electric_Multiple_Unit" class="mw-redirect" title="Electric Multiple Unit">EMU</a> trains, designated Class 373 in the United Kingdom and TGV TMST in France. The units have also been branded as the Eurostar e300 by Eurostar since 2015. There are two variants:\n</p>\n<ul><li>31 "Inter-Capital" sets consisting of two <a href="/wiki/Power_car" title="Power car">power cars</a> and eighteen passenger carriages. These trains are 394 metres (1,293&#160;ft) long and can carry 750 passengers: 206 in first class, 544 in standard class.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>7 shorter "North of London" sets which have two <a href="/wiki/Power_car" title="Power car">power cars</a> and fourteen passenger carriages and are 320 metres (1,050&#160;ft) long. These sets have a capacity of 558 seats: 114 first class, 444 standard and which were designed to operate the aborted <a href="/wiki/Regional_Eurostar" title="Regional Eurostar">Regional Eurostar</a> services.</li></ul>\n<p>The trains are essentially modified <a href="/wiki/TGV" title="TGV">TGV</a> sets,<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> and can operate at up to 300 kilometres per hour (186&#160;mph) on high-speed lines, and 160 kilometres per hour (100&#160;mph) in the Channel Tunnel.<sup id="cite_ref-railfaneurostar_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-railfaneurostar-61">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-eurotunnrules_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eurotunnrules-62">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> It is possible to exceed the 300&#160;km/h speed limit, but only with special permission from the safety authorities in the respective country.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup>\nSpeed limits in the Channel Tunnel are dictated by air-resistance, energy (heat) dissipation and the need to be used with other, slower trains. The trains were designed with Channel Tunnel safety in mind, and consist of two independent "half-sets" each with its own power car.<sup id="cite_ref-CTRLrailtec_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CTRLrailtec-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-eurotunnrules_62-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eurotunnrules-62">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> In the event of a serious fire on board while travelling through the tunnel, passengers would be transferred into the undamaged half of the train, which would then be detached and driven out of the tunnel to safety.<sup id="cite_ref-highspeedwho_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-highspeedwho-181">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup>\nIf the undamaged part were the rear half of the train, this would be driven by the Chef du Train, who is a fully authorised driver and occupies the rear driving cab while the train travels through the tunnel for this purpose.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As 27 of the 31 Inter-Capital sets are sufficient to operate the service, four are currently used by SNCF for domestic TGV services; one of these regularly operates a Paris\xe2\x80\x93Lille shuttle. The Eurostar logos have been removed from these sets, but the base colours of white, black, and yellow remain. SNCF\'s lease of the sets is scheduled to last until 2011<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The date of the event predicted near this tag has passed. (February 2014)">needs update</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>, with an option for a further two years.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Each train has a unique four-digit number starting with "3" (3xxx). This designates the train as a Mark 3 TGV (Mark 1 being <a href="/wiki/SNCF_TGV_Sud-Est" title="SNCF TGV Sud-Est">SNCF TGV Sud-Est</a>; Mark 2 being <a href="/wiki/SNCF_TGV_Atlantique" title="SNCF TGV Atlantique">SNCF TGV Atlantique</a>). The second digit denotes the country of ownership:\n</p>\n<ul><li>3<b>0</b>xx UK</li>\n<li>3<b>1</b>xx Belgium</li>\n<li>3<b>2</b>xx France</li>\n<li>3<b>3</b>xx Regional Eurostar</li></ul>\n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Fleet_updates">Fleet updates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Fleet updates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eurostar_Leisure_Select_Seats.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Eurostar_Leisure_Select_Seats.jpg/220px-Eurostar_Leisure_Select_Seats.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Eurostar_Leisure_Select_Seats.jpg/330px-Eurostar_Leisure_Select_Seats.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Eurostar_Leisure_Select_Seats.jpg/440px-Eurostar_Leisure_Select_Seats.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eurostar_Leisure_Select_Seats.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Interior of a <i>Leisure Select</i> Eurostar carriage</div></div></div>\n<p>In 2004\xe2\x80\x932005 the "Inter-Capital" sets still in daily use for international services were refurbished with a new interior designed by <a href="/wiki/Philippe_Starck" title="Philippe Starck">Philippe Starck</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Eurost_His_4-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eurost_His-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup>\nThe original grey-yellow scheme in Standard class and grey-red of First/Premium First were replaced with a grey-brown look in Standard and grey-burnt-orange in First class. Power points were added to seats in First class and coaches 5 and 14 in Standard class. Premium First class was renamed BusinessPremier.\n</p><p>In 2008, Eurostar announced that it would be carrying out a mid-life refurbishment of its Class 373 trains to allow the fleet to remain in service beyond 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup>\nThis will include the 28 units making up the Eurostar fleet, but not the three Class 373/1 units used by SNCF or the seven Class 373/2 "North of London" sets.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup>\nAs part of the refurbishment, the Italian company <a href="/wiki/Pininfarina" title="Pininfarina">Pininfarina</a> was contracted to redesign the interiors,<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> and The Yard Creative was selected to design the new buffet cars.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup>\nOn 11 May 2009 Eurostar revealed the new look for its first-class compartments.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup>\nThe first refurbished train was due in service in 2012,<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> and Eurostar plans to have completed the entire process by 2014.\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<p>On 13 November 2014 Eurostar announced the first refurbished trains would not re-enter the fleet until the 3rd or 4th quarter of 2015 due to delays at the completion centre.\n</p><p>The last refurbished <i>e300</i> re-entered service in April 2019.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Class_374">Class 374</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Class 374">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_374" title="British Rail Class 374">British Rail Class 374</a></div>\n<p>In addition to the announced mid-life update of the existing Class 373 fleet, Eurostar in 2009 reportedly entered prequalification bids for eight new trainsets to be purchased.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> Any new trains would need to meet the same safety rules governing passage through the Channel Tunnel as the existing Class 373 fleet. The replacement to the Class 373 trains has been decided jointly between the French Transport Ministry and the UK <a href="/wiki/Department_for_Transport" title="Department for Transport">Department for Transport</a>.  The new trains will be equipped to use the new <a href="/wiki/ERTMS" class="mw-redirect" title="ERTMS">ERTMS</a> in-cab signalling system, due to be fitted to High Speed 1 around 2040.<sup id="cite_ref-rmtbrist_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rmtbrist-192">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Class_374_in_Paris.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Class_374_in_Paris.jpg/220px-Class_374_in_Paris.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Class_374_in_Paris.jpg/330px-Class_374_in_Paris.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Class_374_in_Paris.jpg/440px-Class_374_in_Paris.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Class_374_in_Paris.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Class 374 at <a href="/wiki/Gare_du_Nord" title="Gare du Nord">Gare du Nord</a> in Paris.</div></div></div>\n<p>On 7 October 2010, it was reported that Eurostar had selected <a href="/wiki/Siemens" title="Siemens">Siemens</a> as preferred bidder to supply 10 <a href="/wiki/Siemens_Velaro" title="Siemens Velaro">Siemens Velaro</a> e320<sup id="cite_ref-rgi320kmhtrains_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rgi320kmhtrains-193">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> trainsets at a cost of \xe2\x82\xac600 million (and a total investment of more than \xc2\xa3700 million with the refurbishment of the existing fleet included)<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> to operate an expanded route network, including services from London to <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a> and <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-rgi20101001_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rgi20101001-195">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> These would be sixteen-car, 400-metre (1,312&#160;ft) long trainsets built to meet current Channel Tunnel regulations.<sup id="cite_ref-rgi20101001_195-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rgi20101001-195">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> The top speed will be 320&#160;km/h (199&#160;mph) and they will have 894\xe2\x80\x93950 seats, unlike the current fleet built by the French company <a href="/wiki/Alstom" title="Alstom">Alstom</a>, which has a top speed of 300&#160;km/h (186&#160;mph) and a seating capacity of 750. Total traction power will be rated at 16 MW.<sup id="cite_ref-rgi320kmhtrains_193-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rgi320kmhtrains-193">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The nomination of Siemens would see it break into the French high-speed market for the first time, as all French and French subsidiary high-speed operators use TGV derivatives produced by <a href="/wiki/Alstom" title="Alstom">Alstom</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> Alstom attempted legal action to prevent Eurostar from acquiring German-built trains, claiming that the Siemens sets ordered would breach Channel Tunnel safety rules,<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup> but this was thrown out of court.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> Alstom said, after its High Court defeat, that it would "pursue alternative legal options to uphold its position". On 4 November 2010, the company lodged a complaint with the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a> over the tendering process, which then asked the British government for "clarification".<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> Alstom then announced it had started legal action against Eurostar, again in the <a href="/wiki/High_Court_of_Justice" title="High Court of Justice">High Court</a> in London.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup>\nIn July 2011, the High Court rejected Alstom\'s claim that the tender process was "ineffective",<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> and in April 2012 Alstom said it would call off pending court actions against Siemens.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup> This effectively freed the way for Siemens to build the new Eurostar trains,<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> the first of which were expected to enter service in late 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (January 2018)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>On 13 November 2014 Eurostar announced the purchase of an additional seven e320s for delivery in the second half of 2016. At the same time, Eurostar announced the first five e320s from the original order of ten would be available by December 2015, with the remaining five entering service by May 2016. Of the five sets ready by December 2015, three of them were planned to be used on London-Paris and London-Brussels routes.<sup id="cite_ref-railwaygazette.com_208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-railwaygazette.com-208">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Past_fleet">Past fleet</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Past fleet">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="wikitable">\n\n<tbody><tr style="background:#f9f9f9;">\n<th rowspan="2">Class\n</th>\n<th rowspan="2">Image\n</th>\n<th rowspan="2">Type\n</th>\n<th colspan="2">Top speed\n</th>\n<th rowspan="2">Number<br />operated\n</th>\n<th rowspan="2">Notes\n</th></tr>\n<tr style="background:#f9f9f9;">\n<th>mph\n</th>\n<th>km/h\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_37" title="British Rail Class 37">Class 37</a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/File:37603_and_37604_At_Clapham_Junction.jpg" class="image"><img alt="37603 and 37604 At Clapham Junction.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/37603_and_37604_At_Clapham_Junction.jpg/100px-37603_and_37604_At_Clapham_Junction.jpg" decoding="async" width="100" height="75" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/37603_and_37604_At_Clapham_Junction.jpg/150px-37603_and_37604_At_Clapham_Junction.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/37603_and_37604_At_Clapham_Junction.jpg/200px-37603_and_37604_At_Clapham_Junction.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Diesel_locomotive" title="Diesel locomotive">Diesel locomotive</a>\n</td>\n<td>90\n</td>\n<td>145\n</td>\n<td>12\n</td>\n<td>Intended to operate sleeper services over non-electrified parts of the railway network in Britain. Eurostar retained three locomotives for the rescue of failed trains, route learning and driver training, but sold them to <a href="/wiki/Direct_Rail_Services" title="Direct Rail Services">Direct Rail Services</a> when the new <a href="/wiki/Temple_Mills_TMD" class="mw-redirect" title="Temple Mills TMD">Temple Mills Depot</a> opened in November 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_73" title="British Rail Class 73">Class 73</a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/File:Class_73s_at_Dereham_in_2008.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Class 73s at Dereham in 2008.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Class_73s_at_Dereham_in_2008.jpg/100px-Class_73s_at_Dereham_in_2008.jpg" decoding="async" width="100" height="75" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Class_73s_at_Dereham_in_2008.jpg/150px-Class_73s_at_Dereham_in_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Class_73s_at_Dereham_in_2008.jpg/200px-Class_73s_at_Dereham_in_2008.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920" /></a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Electro-diesel_locomotive" title="Electro-diesel locomotive">Electro-diesel locomotive</a>\n</td>\n<td>90\n</td>\n<td>145\n</td>\n<td>2\n</td>\n<td>Were used primarily to rescue failed trains. Eurostar operated two of these from its <a href="/wiki/North_Pole_depot" title="North Pole depot">North Pole depot</a> until 2007, when they were loaned to a pair of educational initiatives having become redundant following the move to Temple Mills.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_92" title="British Rail Class 92">Class 92</a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/File:92027_George_Eliot_at_Stafford.jpg" class="image"><img alt="92027 George Eliot at Stafford.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/92027_George_Eliot_at_Stafford.jpg/100px-92027_George_Eliot_at_Stafford.jpg" decoding="async" width="100" height="75" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/92027_George_Eliot_at_Stafford.jpg/150px-92027_George_Eliot_at_Stafford.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/92027_George_Eliot_at_Stafford.jpg/200px-92027_George_Eliot_at_Stafford.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Electric_locomotive" title="Electric locomotive">Electric locomotive</a>\n</td>\n<td>87\n</td>\n<td>140\n</td>\n<td>7\n</td>\n<td>Intended to operate the <a href="/wiki/Nightstar_(train)" title="Nightstar (train)">Nightstar</a> sleeper services. Eurostar owned seven units of this class, which never saw service until they were sold in 2007 to <a href="/wiki/Europorte_2" class="mw-redirect" title="Europorte 2">Europorte 2</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_373" title="British Rail Class 373">Class 373 <i>Eurostar e300</i></a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/File:Eurostar_sets_3206_3205_at_Ashford_international_14961954169.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Eurostar sets 3206 3205 at Ashford international 14961954169.jpg" decoding="async" width="100" height="57" 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Eurostar_sets_3206_3205_at_Ashford_international_14961954169.jpg/200px-Eurostar_sets_3206_3205_at_Ashford_international_14961954169.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4278" data-file-height="2444" /></a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Electric_multiple_unit" title="Electric multiple unit">EMU</a>\n</td>\n<td>186\n</td>\n<td>300\n</td>\n<td>26\n</td>\n<td>9 in storage, 4 preserved and 13 scrapped\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Possible_use_of_double-deck_trains">Possible use of double-deck trains</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Possible use of double-deck trains">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 2005, the chief executive of Eurostar, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Brown_(transport)" class="mw-redirect" title="Richard Brown (transport)">Richard Brown</a>, suggested that existing Eurostar trains could be replaced by <a href="/wiki/Bilevel_rail_car" title="Bilevel rail car">double-deck trains</a> similar to the <a href="/wiki/SNCF_TGV_Duplex" title="SNCF TGV Duplex">TGV Duplex units</a> when they are withdrawn from service. According to Brown, a double-deck fleet could carry 40&#160;million passengers per year from Britain to <a href="/wiki/Continental_Europe" title="Continental Europe">Continental Europe</a>, equivalent to adding an extra runway at a London airport.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span id="Accidents.2C_incidents_and_events"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Accidents,_incidents_and_events">Accidents, incidents and events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Accidents, incidents and events">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>A number of technical incidents have affected Eurostar services over the years, but up to the present<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> there has only been one major accident involving a service operated by Eurostar, a derailment in June 2000. Other incidents in the Channel Tunnel \xe2\x80\x93 such as the <a href="/wiki/1996_Channel_Tunnel_fire" title="1996 Channel Tunnel fire">1996</a> and <a href="/wiki/2008_Channel_Tunnel_fire" title="2008 Channel Tunnel fire">2008 Channel Tunnel fires</a> \xe2\x80\x93 have affected Eurostar services but were not directly related to Eurostar\'s operations. However, the breakdowns in the tunnel, which resulted in cessation of service and inconvenience to thousands of passengers, in the run-up to Christmas 2009, proved a public-relations disaster.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Minor_incidents">Minor incidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Minor incidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>There have been several minor incidents with a few Eurostar services. In October 1994 there were teething problems relating to the start of operations. The first preview train, carrying 400&#160;members of the press and media, was delayed for two hours by technical problems.<sup id="cite_ref-Eurobreakdown_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eurobreakdown-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-TGVwebaccid_215-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TGVwebaccid-215">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup>\nOn 29 May 2002 a Eurostar train was initially sent down a wrong line \xe2\x80\x93 towards <a href="/wiki/London_Victoria_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="London Victoria railway station">London Victoria railway station</a> instead of London Waterloo \xe2\x80\x93 causing the service to arrive 25&#160;minutes late. A signalling error that led to the incorrect routeing was stated to have caused "no risk" as a result.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 11 April 2006, a house collapsed next to a railway line near London which caused Eurostar services to have to terminate and start from Ashford International instead of London Waterloo. Passengers waiting at Waterloo International were initially directed on to local trains towards Ashford leaving from the adjacent <a href="/wiki/London_Waterloo_East_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="London Waterloo East railway station">London Waterloo East railway station</a>, until overcrowding occurred at Ashford.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1996">1996</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: 1996">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Approximately 1,000 passengers were trapped in darkness for several hours inside two Eurostar trains on the night of 19/20 February 1996. The trains stopped inside the tunnels due to electronic failures caused by snow and ice. Questions were raised at the time about the ability of the train and tunnel electronics to withstand the mix of snow, salt and ice which collect in the tunnels during periods of extreme cold.<sup id="cite_ref-snow1996_220-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-snow1996-220">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2000">2000</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: 2000">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 5 June 2000 a Eurostar train travelling from Paris to London derailed on the <a href="/wiki/LGV_Nord" title="LGV Nord">LGV Nord</a> high-speed line while traveling at 290&#160;km/h (180&#160;mph). Fourteen people were treated for light injuries or shock, with no fatalities or major injuries. The articulated nature of the trainset was credited with maintaining stability during the incident and all of the train stayed upright.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup> The incident was caused by a traction link on the second bogie of the front power car coming loose, leading to components of the transmission system on that bogie impacting the track.<sup id="cite_ref-TGVwebaccid_215-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TGVwebaccid-215">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2007">2007</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: 2007">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The first departures from St Pancras on 14 November 2007 coincided with an open-ended strike by French rail unions as part of <a href="/wiki/November_2007_strikes_in_France" title="November 2007 strikes in France">general strike actions</a> over proposed public-sector pension reforms. The trains were operated by uninvolved British employees and service was not interrupted.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc20071114_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc20071114-72">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2009">2009</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: 2009">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 23 September 2009 an overhead power line dropped on to a Class 373 train arriving at St Pancras station, activating a circuit breaker and delaying eleven other trains.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup> Two days later, on 25 September 2009, electrical power via the overhead lines was lost on a section of high-speed line outside Lille, delaying passengers on two evening Eurostar-operated services.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/December_2009_European_snowfall" class="mw-redirect" title="December 2009 European snowfall">December 2009 European snowfall</a>, five Eurostar trains broke down inside the <a href="/wiki/Channel_Tunnel" title="Channel Tunnel">Channel Tunnel</a>, after leaving France, and one in Kent on 18 December. Although the trains had been <a href="/wiki/Winterization" title="Winterization">winterised</a>, the systems had not coped with the conditions.<sup id="cite_ref-tel1_224-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tel1-224">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> Over 2,000 passengers were stuck inside failed trains inside the tunnel, and over 75,000 had their services disrupted.<sup id="cite_ref-fig2_225-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fig2-225">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup> All Eurostar services were cancelled from Saturday 19 December to Monday 21 December 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup> An independent review, published on 12 February 2010, was critical of the contingency plans in place for assisting passengers stranded by the delays, calling them "insufficient".<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2010">2010</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: 2010">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 7 January 2010 a Brussels-London train broke down in the Channel Tunnel,<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup> resulting in three other trains failing to complete their journeys.<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup> The cause of the failure was the onboard signalling system.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup> Due to the severe weather, a limited service was operated in the next few days.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 15 February 2010, services between Brussels and London were interrupted following the <a href="/wiki/Halle_train_collision" title="Halle train collision">Halle train collision</a>, this time after the dedicated <a href="/wiki/HSL_1" title="HSL 1">HSL 1</a> lines in the suburbs of the Belgian capital were blocked by debris from a serious train crash on the suburban commuter lines alongside.<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup> No efforts were made to reroute trains around the blockage; Eurostar instead terminated services to Brussels at Lille, directing passengers to continue their journey on local trains. Brussels services resumed on a limited scale on 22 February.\n</p><p>On 21 February 2010 the 21:43 service from Paris to London broke down just outside Ashford International,<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup> stranding 740 passengers for several hours while a rescue train was called in.\n</p><p>On 15 April 2010 <a href="/wiki/Air_travel_disruption_after_the_2010_Eyjafjallaj%C3%B6kull_eruption" title="Air travel disruption after the 2010 Eyjafjallaj\xc3\xb6kull eruption">air traffic in Western Europe closed</a> because of the <a href="/wiki/2010_eruptions_of_Eyjafjallaj%C3%B6kull" title="2010 eruptions of Eyjafjallaj\xc3\xb6kull">eruption</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Eyjafjallaj%C3%B6kull" title="Eyjafjallaj\xc3\xb6kull">Eyjafjallaj\xc3\xb6kull</a> volcano. Many travellers between the UK and the European mainland instead took the Eurostar train, all tickets between Brussels and London on 15 and 16 April being sold out within 3\xc2\xbd hours after the closure of British airspace.\n<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup> Between 15 and 20 April, Eurostar put on 33 additional trains and carried 165,000 passengers \xe2\x80\x93 50,000 more than had been scheduled to travel during this period.\n</p><p>On 20 December 2010, the Channel Tunnel was closed off for a day due to snowy weather. Eurostar Trains were suspended that day with thousands of passengers stranded in the run up to Christmas.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2011">2011</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: 2011">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 17 October 2011 a man fell from the 17:04 service from London to Brussels as it passed through Westenhanger and Cheriton in Folkestone, near the entry to the Channel Tunnel.<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup> The individual was an Albanian who had been refused entry to the United Kingdom and was voluntarily returning to Brussels. He was pronounced dead at the scene. The line was closed for several hours following the incident.<sup id="cite_ref-door-death-railnetwork_238-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-door-death-railnetwork-238">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup> The train itself returned north to Ashford International, where passengers were transferred to a Eurostar service operating from Marne-la-Vall\xc3\xa9e to London.<sup id="cite_ref-door-death-railnetwork_238-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-door-death-railnetwork-238">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Possible_developments">Possible developments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Possible developments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Stratford_International_station">Stratford International station</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Stratford International station">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Eurostar trains do not currently call at <a href="/wiki/Stratford_International_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Stratford International railway station">Stratford International</a>, originally intended to be the London stop for the regional Eurostars.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup> This was to be reviewed following the 2012 Olympics.<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup> However, in 2013, Eurostar claimed that its \'business would be hit\' by stopping trains there.<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Regional_Eurostar">Regional Eurostar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Regional Eurostar">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Regional_Eurostar" title="Regional Eurostar">Regional Eurostar</a></div>\n<p>Although the original plan for Regional Eurostar services to destinations north of London was abandoned,<sup id="cite_ref-regionfail_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-regionfail-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> the significantly improved journey times available since the opening of <a href="/wiki/High_Speed_1" title="High Speed 1">High Speed 1</a> \xe2\x80\x94 which is physically connected to both the <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_Main_Line" title="East Coast Main Line">East Coast Main Line</a> and the <a href="/wiki/North_London_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="North London Line">North London Line</a> (for the <a href="/wiki/West_Coast_Main_Line" title="West Coast Main Line">West Coast Main Line</a>) at <a href="/wiki/London_St_Pancras_International" class="mw-redirect" title="London St Pancras International">London St Pancras International</a> \xe2\x80\x93 and the recently<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (August 2019)">when?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> increased maximum speeds on the West Coast Main Line may make potential Regional Eurostar services more commercially viable. This would be even more likely if proposals are adopted for a new high-speed line from London to the north of Britain.<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup>\nSimon Montague, Eurostar\'s Director of Communications, commented that: "...International services to the regions are only likely once High Speed 2 is built."<sup id="cite_ref-yorkmonta_243-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yorkmonta-243">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup> However, as of 2014 the current plans for <a href="/wiki/High_Speed_2" title="High Speed 2">High Speed 2</a> do not allow for a direct rail link between that new line, and High Speed 1, meaning passengers would still be required to change at <a href="/wiki/London_Euston" class="mw-redirect" title="London Euston">London Euston</a> and take some form of transportation to <a href="/wiki/London_St_Pancras_International" class="mw-redirect" title="London St Pancras International">London St Pancras International</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Key pieces of infrastructure still belong to LCR via its subsidiary London &amp; Continental Stations and Property, such as the <a href="/wiki/Manchester_International_Depot" title="Manchester International Depot">Manchester International Depot</a>, and Eurostar (UK) still owns several track access rights and the rights to paths on both the <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_Main_Line" title="East Coast Main Line">East Coast Main Line</a> and the <a href="/wiki/West_Coast_Main_Line" title="West Coast Main Line">West Coast Main Line</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-orr_245-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-orr-245">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nr_246-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nr-246">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup>\nWhile no announcement has been made of plans to start Regional Eurostar services, it remains a possibility for the future. In the meantime, the closest equivalent to Regional Eurostar services are same-station connections with <a href="/wiki/East_Midlands_Railway" title="East Midlands Railway">East Midlands Railway</a> and <a href="/wiki/Govia_Thameslink_Railway" title="Govia Thameslink Railway">Thameslink</a>, changing at <a href="/wiki/London_St_Pancras_International" class="mw-redirect" title="London St Pancras International">London St Pancras International</a>. The construction of a new concourse at adjacent <a href="/wiki/London_King%27s_Cross_railway_station" title="London King&#39;s Cross railway station">London King\'s Cross</a> improved interchange with St Pancras and provided <a href="/wiki/London_North_Eastern_Railway" title="London North Eastern Railway">London North Eastern Railway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Govia_Thameslink_Railway" title="Govia Thameslink Railway">Great Northern</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hull_Trains" title="Hull Trains">Hull Trains</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grand_Central_(train_operating_company)" title="Grand Central (train operating company)">Grand Central</a> services with easier connections to Eurostar.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="High_Speed_2">High Speed 2</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: High Speed 2">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Pancras_Eurostars.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/St_Pancras_Eurostars.jpg/220px-St_Pancras_Eurostars.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/St_Pancras_Eurostars.jpg/330px-St_Pancras_Eurostars.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/St_Pancras_Eurostars.jpg/440px-St_Pancras_Eurostars.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1088" data-file-height="744" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Pancras_Eurostars.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Several Eurostar trains in <a href="/wiki/St_Pancras_International_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="St Pancras International railway station">St Pancras International railway station</a></div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/High_Speed_2" title="High Speed 2">High Speed 2</a></div>\n<p>Eurostar has already been involved in reviewing and publishing reports into High Speed 2 for the British Government<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup> and looks favourably upon such an undertaking. The operation of Regional Eurostar services will not be considered until such time as High Speed 2 has been completed.<sup id="cite_ref-yorkmonta_243-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yorkmonta-243">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup> Alternatively, future loans of the North of London sets to other operators would enable the trains to operate at their full speed, unlike <a href="/wiki/Great_North_Eastern_Railway" title="Great North Eastern Railway">GNER\'s</a> previous loan between 2000 and 2005, where the trains were limited to 175&#160;km/h (109&#160;mph) on regular track.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="LGV_Picardie">LGV Picardie</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: LGV Picardie">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/LGV_Picardie" title="LGV Picardie">LGV Picardie</a></div>\n<p>LGV Picardie is a proposed high-speed line between Paris and Calais via <a href="/wiki/Amiens" title="Amiens">Amiens</a>. By cutting off the corner of the LGV Nord at Lille, it would enable Eurostar trains to save 20&#160;minutes on the journey between Paris and Calais, bringing the London\xe2\x80\x93Paris journey time under 2&#160;hours. In 2008 the French Government announced its future investment plans for new LGVs to be built up to 2020; LGV Picardie was not included but was listed as planned in the longer term.<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="New_destinations">New destinations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: New destinations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Operational_difficulties_with_cross-border_trains">Operational difficulties with cross-border trains</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Operational difficulties with cross-border trains">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="quotebox pullquote floatright" style="width:25%; ;"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1012376600">.mw-parser-output .quotebox{background-color:#F9F9F9;border:1px solid #aaa;box-sizing:border-box;padding:10px;font-size:88%;max-width:100%}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft{margin:0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright{margin:0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.centered{margin:0.5em auto 0.8em auto}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft p,.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright p{font-style:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-title{background-color:#F9F9F9;text-align:center;font-size:larger;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:before{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" \xe2\x80\x9c ";vertical-align:-45%;line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:after{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" \xe2\x80\x9d ";line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .left-aligned{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .right-aligned{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .center-aligned{text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .quotebox cite{display:block;font-style:normal}@media screen and (max-width:640px){.mw-parser-output .quotebox{width:100%!important;margin:0 0 0.8em!important;float:none!important}}</style>\n<div class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">"We know we can go to most places in France physically, because our trains are compatible with French infrastructure, but then you\'ve got to look at impact on fleet utilisation, you\'ve got to have a station that\'s got the spare capacity to have a train stood for a number of hours, for all the security, screening, passport control passes. So it\'s not possible to go just anywhere. And you\'ve got to be able to get the control authorities to agree that there\'s a big enough market for it to be worthwhile for them to set up there."</div>\n<p><cite class="left-aligned" style=""><small>Richard Brown, Chief Executive of Eurostar.<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup></small></cite>\n</p>\n</div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eurostars_373_210_and_373_205_Brussels-South,_June_2014.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Eurostars_373_210_and_373_205_Brussels-South%2C_June_2014.JPG/220px-Eurostars_373_210_and_373_205_Brussels-South%2C_June_2014.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Eurostars_373_210_and_373_205_Brussels-South%2C_June_2014.JPG/330px-Eurostars_373_210_and_373_205_Brussels-South%2C_June_2014.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Eurostars_373_210_and_373_205_Brussels-South%2C_June_2014.JPG/440px-Eurostars_373_210_and_373_205_Brussels-South%2C_June_2014.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3776" data-file-height="2520" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eurostars_373_210_and_373_205_Brussels-South,_June_2014.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Eurostar <i>e300</i> trains, in their former livery at <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Midi" class="mw-redirect" title="Brussels Midi">Brussels Midi/Zuid/South</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The reduced journey times offered by the opening of High Speed 1<sup id="cite_ref-alstomhs1_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alstomhs1-73">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> and the opening of the <a href="/wiki/LGV_Est" title="LGV Est">LGV Est</a> and <a href="/wiki/HSL-Zuid" title="HSL-Zuid">HSL-Zuid</a> bring more <a href="/wiki/Continental_Europe" title="Continental Europe">continental</a> destinations<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup>\nwithin a range from London where rail is competitive with air travel. By Eurostar\'s estimates a train would then take 3 hours 30 minutes from London to Amsterdam.<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup>\nAt present Eurostar is concentrating on developing its connections with other services,<sup id="cite_ref-bahneuroally_101-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bahneuroally-101">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ThalesEuro_102-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ThalesEuro-102">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> but direct services to other destinations would be possible. With the new e320 rolling stock allowed Eurostar to enter the Netherlands and possibly Germany in future. In additional with every new country Eurostar enters there are security issues, due to the UK\'s not having signed up to the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Agreement" title="Schengen Agreement">Schengen Agreement</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Schengen_108-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schengen-108">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> which allows unrestricted movement across borders of member countries. For example, on the current Amsterdam to London route it is only direct one way, with people needing to get a train to Brussels to go through the <a href="/wiki/Juxtaposed_controls" title="Juxtaposed controls">juxtaposed controls</a>; the direct connection is subject to talks between the UK and Dutch governments, set to be completed in 2020 for services to start.\n</p><p>The difficulties that Eurostar faces in expanding its services would also be faced by any potential competitors to Eurostar. As the UK is outside the Schengen Agreement, London-bound trains must use platforms that are physically isolated,<sup id="cite_ref-highspeedwho_181-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-highspeedwho-181">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> a constraint which other international operators such as Thalys do not face. In addition, the British authorities are required to make passenger security and passport checks before they board the train,<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup>\nwhich might deter domestic passengers. Compounding the difficulties in providing a similar service are the Channel Tunnel safety rules, the major ones being the "half-train rule" and the "length rule". The "half-train rule" stipulated that passenger trains had to be able to split in the case of emergency.<sup id="cite_ref-eurotunnrules_62-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eurotunnrules-62">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> Class 373 trains were designed as two half-sets, which when coupled form a complete train, enabling them to be split easily in the event of an emergency while in the tunnel, with the unaffected set able to be driven out. The half-train rule was finally abolished in May 2010. However, the "length rule", which states that passenger trains must be at least 375 metres long with a through corridor (to match the distance between the safety doors in the tunnel), was retained, preventing any potential operators from applying to run services with existing fleets (the majority of both TGV and ICE trains are only 200m long).<sup id="cite_ref-channeltunneligc.co.uk_253-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-channeltunneligc.co.uk-253">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="French_high-speed_rail_expansion">French high-speed rail expansion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: French high-speed rail expansion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Eurostar_expansion">Eurostar expansion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Eurostar expansion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>At the same time as Pepy\'s announcement, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Brown_(transport_executive)" title="Richard Brown (transport executive)">Richard Brown</a> announced that Eurostar\'s plans for expanding its network potentially included <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rotterdam" title="Rotterdam">Rotterdam</a> as destinations, using the <a href="/wiki/HSL_Zuid" class="mw-redirect" title="HSL Zuid">HSL Zuid</a> line. This would require either equipment upgrades of the existing fleet, or a new fleet equipped for both <a href="/wiki/ERTMS" class="mw-redirect" title="ERTMS">ERTMS</a> and the domestic signalling systems used by <a href="/wiki/Nederlandse_Spoorwegen" title="Nederlandse Spoorwegen">Nederlandse Spoorwegen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">&#91;253&#93;</a></sup> Following the December 2009 opening of HSL Zuid, a London\xe2\x80\x93Amsterdam journey is estimated to take 4 hr 16 min.<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">&#91;254&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In an interview with Eurostar\'s Chief Executive <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Petrovic" title="Nicolas Petrovic">Nicolas Petrovic</a> in the <i>Financial Times</i> in May 2012, an intention for Eurostar to serve ten new destinations was expressed, including <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lyon" title="Lyon">Lyon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marseille" title="Marseille">Marseille</a> and <a href="/wiki/Geneva" title="Geneva">Geneva</a>, along with a likely second hub to be created in Brussels.<sup id="cite_ref-odell-expansion_256-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-odell-expansion-256">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">&#91;256&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In March 2016 in an interview with Bloomberg, Eurostar\'s Chief Executive expressed interest in operating a direct train service between London and Bordeaux, but not before 2019. Journey time was said to be around four and a half hours using the new <a href="/wiki/LGV_Sud_Europe_Atlantique" title="LGV Sud Europe Atlantique">LGV Sud Europe Atlantique</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">&#91;257&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Southern_France">Southern France</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Southern France">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>In December 2012 Eurostar announced that on Saturdays during May 2013\xe2\x80\x93June 2013 a new seasonal service would be introduced to <a href="/wiki/Aix-en-Provence_TGV_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Aix-en-Provence TGV railway station">Aix-en-Provence</a>, also serving <a href="/wiki/Lyon_Part-Dieu_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Lyon Part-Dieu railway station">Lyon Part-Dieu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Avignon_TGV" class="mw-redirect" title="Avignon TGV">Avignon TGV</a> on the way (the latter being 6 kilometres (4 miles) from central Avignon). This is in addition to the long-standing seasonal summer service on Saturdays during July and August and the first week of September travelling to <a href="/wiki/Gare_d%27Avignon_Centre" class="mw-redirect" title="Gare d&#39;Avignon Centre">Avignon Centre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Eurostar_new_Provence_services_259-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eurostar_new_Provence_services-259">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup> The Aix-en-Provence services did not run in 2014 but was replaced along with the seasonal Avignon Centre services with the new year-round service to Lyon and Marseille as of 1 May 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-railwaygazette.com_208-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-railwaygazette.com-208">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup>\nIn 2018, at least, direct services to Lyon, Avignon and Marseille ran only from May to September,<sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">&#91;259&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-seat61.com_261-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-seat61.com-261">&#91;260&#93;</a></sup> with connections during the rest of the year being offered via Eurostar but requiring a change to SNCF trains in Paris or Lille.<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">&#91;261&#93;</a></sup> Travel time from London to Marseille was roughly 6.5 hours in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-seat61.com_261-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-seat61.com-261">&#91;260&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Netherlands">Netherlands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: Netherlands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:First_commercial_Eurostar_service_at_Amsterdam_Centraal_station_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/First_commercial_Eurostar_service_at_Amsterdam_Centraal_station_1.jpg/220px-First_commercial_Eurostar_service_at_Amsterdam_Centraal_station_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="168" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/First_commercial_Eurostar_service_at_Amsterdam_Centraal_station_1.jpg/330px-First_commercial_Eurostar_service_at_Amsterdam_Centraal_station_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/First_commercial_Eurostar_service_at_Amsterdam_Centraal_station_1.jpg/440px-First_commercial_Eurostar_service_at_Amsterdam_Centraal_station_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4436" data-file-height="3381" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:First_commercial_Eurostar_service_at_Amsterdam_Centraal_station_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The first Eurostar service from London after its arrival at Amsterdam Centraal, 4 April 2018</div></div></div>\n<p>In September 2013, Eurostar announced an agreement with the Government of Netherlands and NS, the Dutch railway company, to start twice daily services between London and <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Centraal" class="mw-redirect" title="Amsterdam Centraal">Amsterdam Centraal</a>; the launch was initially planned for December 2016. The service will use the newly bought Siemens Velaro trainsets and will also call at Brussels, and Rotterdam. The journey time will be around four hours.<sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263">&#91;262&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Initially, trains stop in Brussels for about half an hour to allow domestic passengers from Amsterdam and Rotterdam to leave and allow London bound passengers to board.<sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">&#91;263&#93;</a></sup> Eventually, Passengers for London from Amsterdam and Rotterdam will undertake all security checks before boarding and will be able to travel direct both ways. The trains will also convey passengers from the Netherlands on journeys to Brussels who will not need to pass through security and they will be allocated half the train which will be kept separate from the London-bound passengers by locking the intermediate door. The Brussels-bound half of the train will be security swept on arrival at Brussels before Brussels-to-London passengers can board.<sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The journey from London to Amsterdam Centraal will take 3 hr 41 min and trains will call at Brussels Zuid/Midi and Rotterdam Centraal Station. From Amsterdam Centraal to London St Pancras, trains will take 4 hr 9 min to include the 28-minute stop at Brussels. Eurostar trains from London will also call at Antwerp Centraal and Schiphol Airport, although trains from Amsterdam will miss out Antwerp on the journey back to London.<sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In November 2014, Eurostar announced the service to Amsterdam would start in "2016-2017", and would include a stop at <a href="/wiki/Schiphol_Airport_railway_station" title="Schiphol Airport railway station">Schiphol Airport</a> in addition to the previously announced destinations. Eurostar have indicated that the calling pattern \'is not set in stone\' and if a business case supports it the service might be extended to additional cities such as Utrecht.<sup id="cite_ref-railnews25052017_267-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-railnews25052017-267">&#91;266&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The service was finally planned to start running on 4 April 2018, with fare prices starting at \xc2\xa335 for a single ticket.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_268-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-268">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup> An "inaugural train" from St Pancras International to Amsterdam via Rotterdam broke a speed record for the journey to Brussels (1hr 46mins) on 20 February 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_268-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-268">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup> The first regular service to Amsterdam left St Pancras at 08:31 on 4 April 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">&#91;268&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The direct Amsterdam to London service is scheduled to launch on 26 October 2020 with two trains a day Monday - Friday.<sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup> Until that date, a change in Brussels for passport controls and security added about an hour to journey time. Eurostar stated that the new journey time to London was about four hours (4h 9m) from Amsterdam, and 3h 29m from Rotterdam.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Competition">Competition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Competition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="box-Update plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="Ambox current red Asia Australia.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_current_red_Asia_Australia.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red_Asia_Australia.svg.png" decoding="async" width="42" height="34" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_current_red_Asia_Australia.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red_Asia_Australia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_current_red_Asia_Australia.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red_Asia_Australia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="360" data-file-height="290" /></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section needs to be <b>updated</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">August 2019</span>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/High_Speed_1#Future_operations" title="High Speed 1">High Speed 1 \xc2\xa7&#160;Future operations</a></div>\n<p>In 2010, international rail travel was liberalised by new <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> directives, designed to break up monopolies in order to encourage competition for services between countries.<sup id="cite_ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271">&#91;270&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">&#91;271&#93;</a></sup> \nThis sparked interest among other companies in providing services in competition to Eurostar and new services to destinations beyond Paris and Brussels. The only rail carrier to formally propose and secure permission for such a service up to now is <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bahn" title="Deutsche Bahn">Deutsche Bahn</a>, which intends to run services between London and Germany and the Netherlands. The sale of High Speed One by the British Government having effectively nationalised LCR in June 2009 is also likely to stimulate competition on the line.<sup id="cite_ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273">&#91;272&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In March 2010, it was announced that Eurotunnel was in discussions with the Intergovernment Commission, which oversees the tunnel, with the aim of amending elements of the safety code governing the tunnel\'s usage. Most saliently, the requirement that trains be able to split within the tunnel and each part of the train be driven out to opposite ends has been removed. However, the proposal to allow shorter trains was not passed.<sup id="cite_ref-channeltunneligc.co.uk_253-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-channeltunneligc.co.uk-253">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup> Eurotunnel Chairman &amp; Chief Executive Jacques Gounon said that he hoped the liberalisation of rules would allow entry into the market of competitors such as Deutsche Bahn. Sources at Eurotunnel suggested that Deutsche Bahn could have entered the market at the timetable change in December 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">&#91;273&#93;</a></sup> This, however, did not happen.\n</p><p>In July 2010 Deutsche Bahn (DB) announced that it intended to make a test run with a high-speed ICE-3MF train through the Channel Tunnel in October 2010 in preparation for possible future operations.<sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-275">&#91;274&#93;</a></sup> The trial ran on 19 October 2010 with a <a href="/wiki/ICE_3#Class_406" title="ICE 3">Class 406</a> ICE train specially liveried with a British "Union flag" decal. The train was then put on display for the press at St Pancras International. However, this is not the class of train that would be used for the proposed service. At the St Pancras ceremony, DB revealed that it planned to operate from London to Frankfurt and Amsterdam (two of the biggest air travel markets in Europe), with trains \'splitting &amp; joining\' in Brussels. It hoped to begin these services in 2013 using <a href="/wiki/Siemens_Velaro#Velaro_D" title="Siemens Velaro">Class 407</a> ICE units, with three trains per day each way\xe2\x80\x94morning, midday and afternoon. Initially the only calling points would be Rotterdam on the way to Amsterdam, and Cologne on the way to Frankfurt. Amsterdam and Cologne would be under four hours from London, Frankfurt around five hours.<sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">&#91;275&#93;</a></sup> DB decided to put this on hold mainly due to advance passport check requirements. DB had hoped that immigration checks could be done on board, but British authorities required immigration and security checks to be done at Lille Europe station, taking at least 30 minutes.<sup id="cite_ref-dowd-bbc-052015_116-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dowd-bbc-052015-116">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In August 2010, <a href="/wiki/Trenitalia" title="Trenitalia">Trenitalia</a> announced its desire to eventually run high-speed trains from Italy to the United Kingdom, using its newly ordered high-speed trains. The trains will be delivered from 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277">&#91;276&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (January 2018)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ridership">Ridership</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: Ridership">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Cumulative ridership since 1994 has reached 190 million, 11 million passengers had used its international services during 2018, the highest ever, a 7% increase on the 10\xc2\xb73 million carried in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">&#91;277&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eurostar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=56" title="Edit section:
